de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform fire cautery on the outer side above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, with one on the right and one on the left, each cautery being as long as the width of a coin; and perform one cautery on the back, or two if necessary; and let the cauteries be flat according to the previous description.
de la marris	"of gout" (maris is an old French term for gout)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When gout is cold and moist and does not allow for conception, and the fluids are corrupted and slow to come out; and when they do come out, there is great pain: then it is necessary that three cauteries be performed around the affected area, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two on the back if necessary; and let the cauteries be flat, as we have said.
de la hainche	"of edema" or "dropsy" (hainche is an old French term for edema)
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When humorous vapors descend to the joint of the hip, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and one sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the separation is visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip joint with a cautery similar to a ring, and mark before the separation around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three cauteries of large olives, and let the cauteries be as deep as all hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip joint and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is treated for this as we have said in the division but the treatment is unsuccessful and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other similar good-working pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, perform the fire cautery; and the types of cautery are according to two methods: namely, heated medical instruments, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the boil's knot three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make a deep and large wound between each cautery the width of a thumb, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a single cautery is performed in the middle on the boil's head, so that there are four in total according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, then cauterize it with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier for the dislocation of the boil; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire boil, and all the thickness of the flesh is burnt.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain is located in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauteries are performed where the patient indicates that the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers wide, slightly to the left; and let the cauteries be knife-shaped, and let all the flesh be burnt; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the bones of the foot or near them, then cauterize it there where they feel the pain with three or four points using the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, then more may be done; and if they know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then perform cautery using the knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on for too long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen several who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled completely, and the foot as well, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. After which they died from a stomach complaint.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, perform cautery on both, in this manner. // And the wise men say in the cauterization of inflammation, of which this is the method, make a such iron and let it be as thick as a small nail of digit, or just a bit less, and let there be interlacing between them with a space of the quantity of a nut; and let the interlacings be opposite each other, and let them be like knots, and there should be one well-made iron handle; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is completely red and starts to drip, then place it on the swollen boil of the patient, and rotate it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one application of the iron and let it rest for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after that, treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) said that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its effect, and indeed it is one of the good cauteries for those who can withstand it, and where it is appropriate to use it.
de la dolor dou dos	of the back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from impact, or from excessive evacuation, or from spread out cold matter, none of these similar things is suitable for cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with fetid pills or other similar things, three lines be signed on the back, in the place where the pain is located, using ink; and in each line, five cauteries or more should be made according to the potency and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made in the shape called "poins"; and if you wish, make three or four cauteries at the middle clavicle in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a stiff neck when they get up, and fear; and you will find in the lower spine of the back and the appearance which comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, then cauterize it with the cautery of this sort according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine evenly. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing two or three lines away, and let the points be close to one another. Afterward, cure the area until it is healed, as we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to gout that is in a swollen nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of joint pain.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When there is joint pain due to moisture that has spread to all members of the body, and when pain occurs in the feet, which physicians call "gout" properly, and when it comes from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, then it can be cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary to cauterize the sole of the foot, let the cautery be done with a pointed instrument. And if the pains come up to the knee and other joints, which happens often, let three or four cauteries be made on each knee on every side, in an olive shape; and if you need more, do so, but do not keep your hand far from the heat of the fire.[1](note: )
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the ankles or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and give medicine. For if you take good care of them and purge fluids, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the opening of an abscess.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an abscess comes to a head and the intestines descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that lighten the belly so that the feces come out of their stomach. Afterwards make them sit on their back between your hands and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has been retracted, and massage it with your fingers, and apply pressure underneath the opening above the bone of the wrist, and in a straight line that is half the size of a circle above the body. Then heat up the cautery iron until it is red hot, which looks like this: [The text includes a symbol for fire or the cautery iron.]
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	...until it turns white and drips pus. Then massage the intestines back into place, and the caregiver should place their hand to ensure that they do not move back. And work well on the thighs of the patient, and place a cushion underneath them, and a sergeant on top of the thighs, and another on the chest who holds the hands. Then apply the cautery iron on the mark with all your might, holding it directly and strongly until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you do; but carefully watch that the abscess does not burst during this process and burns neither the patient nor anyone else.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be fine, according to the measure of eggs, and also large for large people, according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the heat is removed; after cure with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie down for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the buboes do not burst when he takes a mind to move around in chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and let him wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, that he does not exert himself much and guards against excessive consumption of drink and food, and of too loud laughter; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. And I will tell you later the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of abdominal surgery
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, perform one searing with the hot iron according to its size, and let a third of the belly be burned; after cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pronged cautery in this form: ...[Note: The text is cut off at the end, so I can't translate the rest]
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but sign first the joint's location and make a mark along the width above the crack, and another below, and place your hand in the middle of the entire fire-brand. But the first cautery is lighter and more nimble.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to a limb, either from falling or from injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "point" cautery. And let the cautery be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and power, and its location, taking into account twisting and pain. If it heals from the first cautery, that is good; but if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for sometimes it is necessary for it to change to the member that is near it, so you must continue with the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and also the diseases that come from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy. When you see it necessary to cauterize, pay attention if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not worsen or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the patient's body, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, and another towards the front at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and so much that the scabs come out, allowing the vapors of the gross humors to escape; and cauterize the area according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the groins of the chest, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are at the back of the heels; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more cautery you do, the more help you provide, and it benefits them; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because their body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary for the cautery to be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the forms of irons. After the cure, sprinkle the wound with barley flour and honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	I'm not sure I understand the context of the word "de enfleure" in your message. If you are asking for a translation of the French verb "enfler" which means "to swell", here is the translation:
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any limb and is treated by medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then cauterization is done on the limb according to the size of the member; and let the cautery be a little deep in the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes cauterization is done on the hand, foot, and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should interfere if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.

Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has woken up and the means of medicine are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the amount of flesh, until the whiteness is removed and the color changed; then cure it with bran of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of dove and almond, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre (a type of skin ulcer) with cautery involves using a hot iron or other heated instrument to burn and destroy the infected tissue. This was a common medical practice in the Middle Ages as it was believed to remove the corrupt humors and promote healing. After cauterization, the wound would be cleaned and dressed with various medicinal substances such as herbs, oils, and powders to help prevent infection and promote healing. The specific method of cautery used for chancre may have varied depending on the severity of the ulcer and the practitioner's preference.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre begins to appear, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And yet, wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, with the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot spread
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it delays in healing, either because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the water of the sick person when they are infirm (that is to say, too old) and have little blood, or for time; and you wish to hasten its healing: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; after leave it as such. For it will hurry to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this: [shape of the cautery is not provided in the text].
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of the ailment called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the heart, and make the cauteries such that the patient feels them from outside in such a way that the course of the putrefaction is alleviated. Afterward heal it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the healing by fire using iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	There is another kind of illness called "corrodens", which is nothing but an eating away of the limbs, just like fire consumes dry wood. If you see this illness in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then heat up the cauteries, both large and small, according to what is needed for the location where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing of it remain. Then leave it alone for three days, and put soothing ointment on the cauterized areas with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all of the corruption. Afterward, heal with ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh is not born, this is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas. This eating away has sometimes been cured by soothing medicine instead of cautery with fire, but still, cautery with fire is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for soothing medicine in the division: take as much as you need when you require it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of fungi that come between the toes
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Very often, a disease arises in the feet, which we call "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large abscess that wounds the foot. And the cautery for this disease is of two kinds: namely, fire cautery and hot water cautery. The fire cautery is as follows: heat a red-hot iron rod as thin as a pen, made of good metal and of a size that can reach the root of the ababscess from all sides, with sharp edges; then place it very hot on the abscess, turning your hand around the rod until you reach the base of the abscess; leave it there for three days until it begins to rot; then apply a plaster made of crushed unripe grapes with oil, and leave it overnight; the pus will come out and the rod will be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the wound by cleaning away any rotten flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they (abscesses) are located in various parts of the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should use hot water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take a rod of iron or copper, or a pen-shaped instrument, and place the red-hot tip on the abscess, that is to say, powdered verdigris (a medicinal compound); then place the rod so that it surrounds (the abscess) completely, then add some hot water and hold your hand firmly, pressing down while turning so that the edges of the rod come into contact with the root of the abscess and can find a path through the heat to reach the root; allow the patient to endure the biting heat of the water for a while (about an hour); then leave it be and it will detach itself, along with all its roots. Do this repeatedly until all the ones in the body have been treated in this way, then cure the wounds by cleaning away any rotten flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone is trembling from cold nerves or quartan fever or any other cause, then you should apply four or five cauteries to them on the spine at the base of the neck, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the affected area (pez) and one on the stomach using an olive-shaped cautery. This will stop the trembling and speed up recovery from the cold disease.[br]
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes appear on the body, due to negligence, stinking pustules that come from corrupt matter. In this case, it is necessary, at first when they appear, to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: with a subtle cautery made from myrtle wood, whose tip is taken by fire, or from a long aristolochia root, or with a round cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized in the beginning, when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but rather the superfluities from which they come are broken up, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It often happens that there is a large loss of blood from the artery that is cut in an injury or incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is very difficult to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, you must quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very hard until the bleeding stops under your finger and no more blood comes out; then heat various sized olive-shaped cauters over the fire until they are all red; then apply one, large or small according to the wound and the location where the artery is cut, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another cautery quickly from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and ensure no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not yet treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stop blood; and it should be bound and held in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will attempt to stop the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or placing hot objects on it, or similar things, will not succeed if it is not effective.[Reference(s):
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have medicine or mirrors present, then they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press down firmly until it stops bleeding above the wound and above the vein; and they must not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations in advance for what they need of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we have described the operations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed the chapter on head wounds at the beginning up to feet, and I will go in this chapter along the same path so that one may more easily find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to undertake foolish things. For many kinds of people come to be treated, some of whom are so afraid of their illness that they easily die from the violence they find in their disease and the severity of its malice; and one should fear these people.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these, there are some who claim to be healed and say: "wait, I am healed"; and the disease is contemptuous. It is not at all appropriate for you to agree to those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than into your greed, and do not rashly but wisely open up those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain credit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients for their health to be restored; and this will help you establish a good reputation, and glory, and memories of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord grant you good understanding and justice, and if you wish to inspire yourself with the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And so I have organized this chapter by topics, as it is before the chapter on cauteries that I have described from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a swollen head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the delivery is strained too hard against the child's head; and sometimes it happens for no known reason. (My translation)
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death hastened; and therefore it seems to me that it is better to abandon the work in such cures. (My translation)
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child where the head was full of water, and the skull grew thicker each day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture gathers under the bone at the top of the siphac, between the brain and the bone; and the operation is such if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the middle of the head a wide cut; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and here is the shape of the spatula: (My translation)
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form: (My translation)
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are that the corners of the lips open on each side, and water squirts out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not heal: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After the incision, remove all the moisture; then bind the incisions with cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, leaving it like this until the fifth day; then undo it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and leave the head bound as well, and give dry food to the patient with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look for the largest part of the abscess, and where the water has gathered; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes to the right, and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess is open and the collection of water is, and make an incision according to your ability; and take care not to cut the artery; and if there comes a flow of blood, so that the patient dies from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rupture (or, a ruptured joint)
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When someone gets a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or the pis (possibly referring to the urethra), and the illness is chronic, and medical treatment does not help at all, then the last cure is the use of cautery with this: they will burn two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you are about to burn the eyes, the patient should tilt their head back; after that, they should rub their face with a rough cloth until the arteries become visible; then the patient should constrict their neck with a single cloth; then look for where the veins protrude, and the locations of these veins are next to the ears, and they are not recessed; then mark those locations with ink, and burn each one with a sharp scalpel in two parts until the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done at the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see a vein, place the scalpel beneath it and cut above, making two incisions crosswise.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, the blood springs out continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not bleed at a touch, you must measure the distance of three fingers and make an incision to the bone; and the amount of blood that must be released is six "c" (a medieval unit of measurement), and perhaps more or less depending on what the patient can tolerate and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if pus remains on the bone tip, cut it out so that abscesses do not form; then close the wound and bind it, treating it with ointments until it heals.
de emigrainne	The term "de emigrainne" is not clear in Old French. If you meant "migraine," here's a line-by-line translation:
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old-fashioned migraines come with a runny nose, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples, and an ancient craziness of the head and similar things, and he is treated by various medical methods without success, we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them (i.e., arrowheads) is as follows: the patient should shave the hair from their temples and pay attention to the artery that appears in the temple, for it is easily visible due to its pulsation, unless in some men who are overly cold; and if it is not visible, have the patient gently tighten their neck with a cloth. Then, rub the area with a rough cloth and apply hot water to the area until the artery becomes clearly visible. Next, take the spatula of the form described here:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then gently flay the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up with hemostats, and ensure that it is well separated from the underlying tissues on both sides. If the artery is small, use the tip of the forceps to lift it. Then cut the tissue along the edge of the two prongs according to the length of the two incisions. For if it is not properly cut, the blood will not escape completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw blood from the six (veins/incisions), up to three; and if the artery is large, it should be tied in two places with a strong double thread of silk to prevent bleeding before the wound heals, and for the blood to flow out. Then remove the excess tissue between the two ligatures at that very hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize the area with a scalpel cautery up to the bone until the arrowheads are removed; and this is the most difficult operation, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery stops moisture (i.e., bleeding), therefore it is of greater help for moistures (i.e., wounds with excessive bleeding).
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one must fill the wound with old cotton and place well-made bandages; and when they are loosened, they should be cared for using dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until it is healed; and if blood flows from the cut artery as much as you work, then quickly cover it using cautery, or fill the wound with vitriol and strain it with your hand so that the blood stops; and if you do not have this present, then place your finger on the wound until the blood clots, and continuously pour cold water on it until the blood ceases, and strain it as needed; and what is easier and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the wound using this cutting cautery of two parts, but let the cuts be thick to maintain their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a finger's breadth of space between the two knives, and then when you have marked the two places, place the red-hot iron on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the wound in two places; and let them be spaced apart because this cautery is not soldered from one end to the other; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes come down from the veins which are above the forehead, and curing with medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel a pulsating sensation on the forehead as if in trembling; and the eyelids are held tightly shut and moist, such that the eyelashes have fallen off, and the eyelids are heated and reddened from the heat of the tears, then this treatment is required.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancient people called it "cure contuse", and this is what you should do for the patient who has this disease: have them shave their forehead, then make three equal incisions on the forehead according to its length; and let one of the incisions be in the middle of the forehead, going down to the nose, and the other two along the temples above the eyelids, and be careful not to cut the arteries which are above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be the width of three fingers together.[translated with help from DeepL](https://www.deepl.com/translator)
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then insert the spatula which is cut in two parts as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is near the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the two incisions right up to the suture that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove the spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if insert into the first wound the instrument called "cultellaria," and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is soft, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the sharp edge towards the fleshy part near the heart, and the blunt edge towards the bone, pushing it until it reaches the middle of the wound. Cut all the blood vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, making an incision continuous down to where the heart is visible, then make another cut in the middle of the wound down to the other side; and then let out the blood equally, squeezing out any remaining with pressure; then place a piece of old cotton in each wound, and cover it with wet cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar, and ensure no pus develops; on the third day loosen the binding, and apply a lotion made from tepid water, followed by treatment with basilicon ointment and other cures used for treating wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the network of veins around the eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a person is accustomed to getting catarrh frequently, and you notice the eyes are sunken and small, with weakened vision and burned paper-like skin; and their hair falls out, and they experience deep pain in the head, along with sneezing; then know from these symptoms that those substances and catarrh do not come from just one vein, but rather many, and the treatment for it is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And instruct the patient to bend their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another of about one inch. Begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and have it go down to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the incision and place a piece of old cotton, and bandage it with linen; then bind damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, and be careful not to cause a hot abscess; once removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying agents that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of flower of wheat and four parts of colophony, and make it into an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to promote the growth of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	for stopping up ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls in ears is one of four things: grains or animals, stone from mines or similar things such as iron; or seeds such as pus, beans, peas; or liquids such as water and earwax and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear a stone or any other thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, place the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, distill a drop of violet oil or oil of cedar, then attempt extraction; and make him sneeze using drugs, and stop up his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upward. This cure often works; and if it does not work, attempt extraction using subtle tweezers, of which this is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, attempt extraction using a thin wire hook; and if it does not come out this way either, then make a small silver tube and insert the end of the tube into the ear hole, and stop up the area around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull it out strongly, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime with which birds are caught, and place some on an instrument made for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all the things we have mentioned, then quickly make an incision in the ear so that abscess and callus may not form, and spasms; and the manner of the incision should be such that you first bleed the patient from the head, and draw blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area; and let the incision be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck on it with your mouth; and continue this treatment until it has healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and has become swollen, then attempt extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin probe according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and make an incision on that swelling. But do not do so when you think that the swelling is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with delicate tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	And in the case of water that falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing with previous conditions, and widen the ear with soft cotton. And lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this means, it is good. If not, take many small and light pebbles, and heat them a little in the fire; and put one of these stones into the patient's ear, and jump on the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out completely; and if you see, take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and light the other end with fire until the thickest part of the reed is burned; then do the same thing again with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it has a small body, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then make an extraction with tweezers; and this is one of the easiest things to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ear, when you cure it as we have said in division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then look at the ear in the sun: if it appears that there are any worms, then extract them with delicate tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take a cane of the kind described below:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let it be tight down below and wide above. And insert the slenderest tip into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then pull the entire canal strongly; do this frequently until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey in coming out, then stop up around the canal with cotton as I have said in the previous passage; and if they still do not come out as we have mentioned, then administer the infusions that the ancients have tested in cases of worms, which you will find in the treatment of infusions; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, such is the method as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or brass, narrow down below with a small hole, and wide above for distillation; and have a well-made brass instrument to press in the distillation, and if you wish take a lancet and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour in your oil or juice, and what you wish of your medicines into the canal, while it is in the ear; then insert the lancet with all the cotton, and press gently with your hand until the oil is distilled or reaches the eardrum; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the tip of the distillation be slightly warmed by fire before distilling into the ear; and make sure that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on the stoppage of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have any holes in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults through blockage from wounds or flesh grown inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes occur deep within the ear where they cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a pouch visible outside the hole.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then, the one that comes deep, if it cannot be seen, is of difficult healing in many ways; and in the one that can be seen, it is necessary that you place the sick person's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the swelling apparent, work on it immediately with this instrument, according to its shape.
