Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and blunt at the front and back, so that it does not wound the ear; if the swelling is in the flesh or core of the ear, hold it with delicate pincers and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the swelling is deep within the ear, take a delicate and sharp lancet, heat it slightly by the fire, then place it in the core of the ear. If you feel the swelling, which causes pain for the patient upon hearing, make a small puncture but be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a wick according to the width of the opening and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound heals or take a wick and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top; and if you see the ear swelling, then you must remove the wick and replace it with another one moistened in an ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue to care for it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if flowing of blood occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the flow of blood, which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	The translation of "de la char des papieres" would be "of the pulp of paper".
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eye-salve that comes in paper, when it is moist and dry, you should stretch it with tongs and forceps, and cut off a piece of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood flows from it (the eye), cauterize it with a subtle circular cautery, and then the cauterizer should move the incision; and many times they (the eyes) recover, as long as anything remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, those roots are destroyed and do not return.
de la gresle	The translation of "de la gresle" is "of hail". This term is used to describe a medical condition caused by hailstorms. In medieval medicine, it was believed that being caught in a hailstorm could cause injury or illness, and specific remedies were recommended for treating these conditions. The text you provided describes the use of a cautery to treat an eye affected by a hailstorm.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come from the eyelids small things that resemble grains in their form and hardness, and this is why this disease is called "hail", and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper of
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the "hail" is going down inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and stretch the hail with pincers, and cut it off and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it doesn't matter; and when the hail is cut off, rinse the eye with salty water, and cure the wound of whatever causes injury until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyelids.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a type of fat that forms in the membranes of the eyelids, and this happens more often in children than in adults, and it greatly bothers their eyes, and they get runny noses in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they lie on their backs with their faces up and sleep, and their eyelids are moist under their eyebrows where the exinach appears in the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers, you can feel it coming out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient places their head on your support; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains pus from each part, then place it on top of it; and press with your hands from one side and the other, so that the pus is gathered within the circle; then make in the middle of the moist area with a sharp blade a slit of a width, and let it not be any larger than the wound that is made when opening a vein; and make the incision deep enough to reach the abscess; and in several ways, the abscess comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then pull out a piece of cloth charpit between your fingers and spread it apart; and make sure not to press on the slit or come at all to the sharp blade until you reach its tip, so that you do not wound yourself.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the abscess does not appear at the beginning of the slit, then slightly increase the size of the incision until it becomes visible; then remove it as we have said, then moisten a cloth with oil and water and place it on top; and bind it with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who crush soil and place it on top to corrupt the moisture that has remained. Then heal it until it is healed. And if it comes to the place abscess hot, so cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs of papers (not sure what this refers to, but based on context I will translate as:)
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on papers unlike what is natural, and they are neglected, they harm the eyes, and bring about various illnesses such as customary tears and softening of the papers and albumin, to the point of causing eye destruction; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine according to what is before the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by caustics, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, so put a needle with one thread on it; and let this be beside the margin of the paper where the hairs grow near these hairs, and pull one thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision beneath the paper, beneath the unnatural hairs, up to the entire spatulum, from the large tear duct down to the small one; then remove one thread, and place underneath the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then lay upon the paper a figure of ink, such as the leaf of myrtle, but it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you wish to raise the elevated paper, which is determined in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if some need a great quantity of paper to be cut according to the softness of the paper; then make an incision along the whole spatula on the two lines that you have marked, and begin at the large tear down to small; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the probe into one of the two corners of the wound, then flay it all; then bring the two lips together with a stitch of a needle with one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and let the surplus of the threads dry on the two eyebrows along with some sticky things, if you wish to do so; and if not, then pay no attention to it, then leave the stitch and threads for 3 or 4 days; then cure the wound without drying or constricting things, for the paper will swell with the healing of the wound and bring it together, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients said), and this is a fearless operation;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And in another way: it is that you mark the paper with a figure that is similar to the leaf of myrtle, as we have told, with three incisions separated according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what overcomes it with small forces equally according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put another thread next to the large tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and bring the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have told, then bring the two lips of the wound together with a stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar calming ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the skin are turned; you should then use what we have said about incisions; but stitches in one and the other are more delicate.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of veins is as follows: you should turn the skin and make an incision as I have said, then make two sutures carefully, and two fine threads as long as the skin and as wide as the width of the spatula; and cut the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then carefully bring the one and the other together on top of the paper above the eye, and pull the two sutures from the two parts firmly; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin which has been pulled will die, turn black, and rot until it falls off.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, cut it again with force, then cure it until it heals; and when the wound is healed, and the skin has lifted, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the two sutures you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is as follows: take a thin needle and thread a soft and fine silk thread onto it; then bring the edges together and tie them carefully, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then prepare another fine thread of silk in the case and tie the ends of the thread; then put the patient's head on your sanction; and place it near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is delicate and small work, then quickly insert the needle to the root of the hair adjacent, and make it pass through the skin until you bring it out above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the case, and insert the pulled hairs into the case if there are one or two or three or more; then remove your hand so that the hairs come out fully at the case with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the arrow is treated and the hair does not come out with it, you will pull the arrow beneath its barbs, as much as you have arranged, until the arrow exits the wound above and you see it with your eye; then you will pull the arrow and the barbs, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair dries in its place and the scar forms; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair of natural growth, and lift it with that or let it be, until it is far enough away, and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of eye ulceration
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or ulceration occurs in the eye, it can be of two types: one natural and the other unnatural. It can happen suddenly due to a wound, a cut, or a burn, and similar things.[note]Aleacrati is not a known medical term in modern medicine. However, based on the context, it could refer to an eye condition characterized by some kind of ulceration or inflammation.[/note]
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	The method of treatment for this condition is to lance the abscess, separate its lips, and place inside linen bandages, keeping them in place until it has healed. It is important that you do not use drying or constricting substances in the treatment. If you do, the condition will return worse than before. Instead, use softening agents such as fenugreek; and boil linseed, barley, and linseed oil, add powdered dyallium and heat it in one of the oils, then wrap it in a bandage and treat the eye with it.[note]Dyallium is an antimony compound that was used as a medication in the Middle Ages. It was often used as a diuretic and to treat skin conditions such as ulcers, ringworm, and lice.[/note][Note: The modern medical term for this condition is likely to be different from "aleacrati" or eye ulceration, as these terms are not used in contemporary medicine. If you have concerns about your eyes or any symptoms you are experiencing, it's important to consult a healthcare professional for an accurate diagnosis and treatment plan.]
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your care is that you ensure it does not heal according to the shape it was before; and these works that we have mentioned are none except remedies for this disease, so that it does not heal according to the shape it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is under the eye, which is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural as well as accidental. The accident comes from wound or fissure, cautery, and similar things; and the method of this work in it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come in two parts of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above over the entire needle, and cut it with a spatula about one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two incisions or cuts inside the paper; and let the holes of the two incisions be at the two angles of the cut you have made, and make them into two angles so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "Greek J"; then remove the flesh according to the width of its sides which are under the paper, then join the two severed parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with what we have said about softening medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a crack, a suture, or a cautery, then you should make a clean break in the crack below the hairs of the skin, following what is mentioned before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and the work should be done according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters should prepare means to the best of their ability on how to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is required for work and instruments in several dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	This phrase likely refers to "the sharp end of the paper," or more specifically, the edge or point of a piece of paper. The text suggests that this sharp edge is used to make a clean break in the skin crack or wound. In medieval medical texts, it was not uncommon for practitioners to use various sharp objects, such as knives, lancets, or even sharp pieces of glass or metal, to make incisions or cuts in the skin. Here, the use of a sharp piece of paper may be a more gentle or less invasive alternative to these other tools. However, without further context, it is difficult to say for certain what specific role this "sharp end of the paper" plays in the medical procedure described.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in many men in such a way that the paper above is glued to the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, until you cut what is hard on the thin spatula, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient can bear the thin spatula not being too sharp or piercing the eye; and your incision, from which you flay the union, should be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and let this union be healed, and sometimes in the eye put salty water, and raise clear water and bile; then place a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and place wool moistened with egg yolk on the eye; and after three days use of collyrium and other healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	"De l'ungle de l'oeil" means "of the eyelid." The eyelid is a protective flap of skin that covers and protects the eye. It helps to keep the eye moist by spreading tears over the surface of the eye, and it also helps to prevent foreign objects from entering the eye. In medical texts, the eyelid may be referred to as the "palpebra" or "lid." The phrase "de l'ungle de l'oeil" specifically refers to the edge or margin of the eyelid where it meets the eyeball. This area is particularly important for maintaining the health and function of the eye, as it helps to distribute tears and protect the eye from foreign objects. In some medical procedures, the eyelid may need to be treated or manipulated in order to address issues with the eye itself.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail comes in two forms: it is sinewy and resembles a hard callus, and another that is not sinewy, but resembles congealed white moisture, which cannot be touched with iron and pricked with forceps; and one and the other form begins near the outer corner of the eye, and grows bit by bit until it covers the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient should place their head over you, then open their eyes; lift the paper with your hand, then pull the nail with forceps of small doubling, and stretch it out; then take a needle, and put in it one horsehair or cow hair, and one strong thread; and bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, and pierce it all the way through with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it out, and skin the side of the nail that follows the eyelid and the silk to the hair all the way up to the head; then cut away the remaining part at the root of the outer corner of the eye as fine as possible and with small forces, and leave the natural skin or outer corner of the eye, so that the body's tears do not come out through the incision; and sometimes the nail is stretched only to the quick, and to the thread, as we have said; then the skin is removed gently from the entire area as follows:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy tissue and break it, and that the eyelid is not pierced; and after the incision, place a little bit of crushed salt and collyrium made of litharge into the eye, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sinewy and you cannot insert the needle, and the quick cannot be reached, this form of nail is often cured with medicines; and it is born as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then operate on the patient's eye, and take a spatula that is slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee. And if the appearance of the flesh in the corner of the eye interferes with vision causing harm, then suspend it at the eyelid and cut away some but not all of it so that no watery discharge comes from it; then instill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.

de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers. de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket

dou derrompement de toile uvee	of a detached retina.

de la bowe de l’oil	Here's the corrected translation:
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but the bow formed in the eye, appearing like descending water, and it's not actually water; and one way to recognize its appearance is to have the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then hold their head with both of your hands and move it until you see the bow come up to your eyes; then stick it in place and let the light not go down and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it doesn't descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not prepared as we have said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and push on the transparent cornea through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the transparent cornea and the crown until the bow comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or boiled water and honey, into the eye, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have similar instances of the waters (or fluids) in division, and what is required for piercing; and we work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye shut very tightly; then place the paper on the eye at your left hand if the eye is left, or at your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the thickness of a reed in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand until it pierces in the whiteness of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda is at the depth of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the eye; and you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the horned veil, and then put the instrument until it reaches where the water is, and press it down one way after another. If the water descends now, let the patient look before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, and if the water rises again along the second path, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and it no longer rises, then gently remove almagda by turning your hand slightly; and then put in a little bit of gemstone powder, and lift the eye inside. Then place cotton or wet wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg over the eye, and bind it with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, apply common broth with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then only pierce the ligament, and do not go too deep, but make a shallow incision, then put on algim (a type of medicine), as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable sleeping aid, in which they sleep on their back in a dark room; and be devoid of all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then loosen the binding in the same dark room, and test his vision, and have him look at some things, and then replace the binding until the seventh day; and it is not at all suitable to do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but one must lighten this, because the water (body fluids) rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess is about to form, then loosen the eye before the seventh day and direct it towards that which soothes an abscess; and when it has calmed down, then unbind the vision and place on his face a bandage to cover for some days, and always remain in that dark room. And then leave the house little by little, and return to your usual activities; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us who was from Iria (a city in Spain), who told us that in his country they make almagda by piercing, from which one can suck the water, but nevertheless I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know it may see; and they should be made of pure tin:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let their heads be of this same delicacy, and their buttocks have three sharp points.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from (the) nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes different kinds of flesh are born on the nose, among which there are some that resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such ones that have fleshy growths of a violet color, and they also have soft flesh of good color. In this case, of these two kinds of flesh, if it is soft and not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; and clear their nostrils, and pour the eye ointment on those fleshy growths, and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a sharp spatula from one side, until you are certain that all the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with a very fine and light instrument so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, cauterize it quickly to stop the bleeding and remove all the flesh; then pour rosewater, vinegar, or wine on (the nose).
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose does not drain and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; but if the moisture does not drain as it should, know that flesh has grown in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach. In this case, you must insert a fairly thick linen thread and tie it loosely with small knots at intervals of about one digit or less; then place the thread in the patient's nose to the best of their ability, and pull on it while sniffing until it comes through the nose into the mouth. This is something that many children in school do, and it is not difficult for those who want to do it. Then hold the piece of flesh coming out of the nose with one hand, and the piece coming out of the mouth with the other hand, and know which knot has touched the rotten flesh. Continue this until you are sure that the knots have destroyed all the flesh, then remove the thread, wipe away the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all remaining flesh. Then place a piece of wax in the nose for several days until it is healed; and if drying medicines are needed, use them. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And whether it be of silver or bronze, similar to an open lamp, like a funnel, and the spout the same; and if you wish, make a closed funnel, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a sickness is born in the head of the nose, called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible; and therefore you must cut it at the beginning and extract it all, then place on it the cautery or a burning medicine; and if you wait until it has grown large before cutting it, see if it is hard, of a dark color, with little sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is cut once, it can cause great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that you can extract all of it, have the patient empty their stomach and cauterize the area without fear, and cure it with drying and constricting agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn up.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then approximate the two lips to a stitch, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, one must cauterize all the edges of their wound until they heal, then approximate the two lips to a stitch and bind them, and put powder of dragon's blood and ground incense on top of the powders, and place a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster on top, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is to approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men there come within the lips hard abscesses like grains of pepper, smaller and larger; then one must turn the lips and make an incision on each nodule, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply the place after the incision with powdered vitriol until the blood is stopped; and then leave it open to air, and cure the place of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swelling of the flesh occurs on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, letting the pus or blood run out; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccative powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, you should cut it again and cauterize it; it will not come back after cauterization. Here are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, calluses appear on the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, green, and yellow, such that the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; you should make the patient sit between your hands, with their chin in your holy palm, and scrape the visible calluses or teeth until nothing remains; and similarly for any black, green, or yellow stains, as well as for any other discolorations, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is present at the first cleaning, that is good; if not, then start again on the second and third day, continuing to scrape until everything is removed. And know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demands, because the scrapers used to scrape outside the teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; these forms and others should be prepared in advance.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure a toothache, you must delay pulling the tooth as long as possible, because one should not do it hastily; for it is a very serious matter until there is no excuse to pull (the tooth).
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is ready to pull, you should make sure of the decayed tooth. Often it happens that the pain deceived the patient, and he thinks it is in a healthy tooth, and has a good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not go away, for the bad tooth remains, as we have often seen with surgeons; and when you are certain of the decayed tooth, you should cauterize around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum from all sides; then pull it out with your hands or with fine tweezers, pulling firmly at first and then more gently until it is completely loose; then securely clamp the tweezers; and have the patient's head between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After pulling the tooth out straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently push it in on both sides, and move it as you did before. And if the teeth are rotten or crumbled, you must fill them with cloth where the holes are; and clamp them delicately with tweezers, so that they do not break when clamped; and you must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care not to break it and leave a part in the patient's mouth, causing greater pain than the original through the malice of the root. Also, be careful not to act as ignorant surgeons do, who sometimes out of haste and recklessness break the jaw, without achieving what we have described; but instead bring about great illness from the roots that remain or from the broken jaw, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, rinse the area with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply a vitriol paste; and if that does not work, cauterize the wound.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to pull teeth first should have long and thick handles that do not bend when pulling the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of sturdy size so that they do not bend when pulled, and let them be made of good quality iron, and let them have teeth to hold onto wounds.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains when pulling, you should place a piece of cotton soaked in butter on the site for one or two days until the area is softened. Then use forceps called "algefri," which have a shape like a bird's beak; and inside they should be made like a file with this shape: [The provided text appears to describe a medical procedure for dealing with a situation where a tooth root remains after an extraction attempt. The instruction is to apply a piece of cotton soaked in butter on the site for one or two days until it softens, and then use special forceps known as "algefri" which have a bird's beak shape, and inside they should be made like a file with the given shape.]
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots still do not want to come out with all these forceps, then you must cut open all the flesh around the root and apply an instrument called "althali," which is a flat piece of metal with this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and sturdy so that it does not break easily. If the root comes out with this, it's good; if not, then use all the instruments described in the following forms:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps oneself with this instrument that has two branches, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other metal instruments that are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large pliers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments, and also other instruments that are not mentioned; and the wise master subtlely finds his own instrument according to what his work and the illness demands, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity, and one does not break a tooth or other bones, but searches among the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and sturdy to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, let it be all smoothed out with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and similarly in young women, you should determine if the tooth is new-growing and not in its correct position, and cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; but if it is misaligned with the tooth next to it, take this instrument, which has a small hook-like shape, and made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And use the file frequently, day by day, because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the other teeth; and if it appears that the tooth can be filed down, file it with a thin file, such as this one shown in the illustration.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is similar to the files used for making needles; and file down the tooth frequently, day by day, gently so that it does not move until it falls out; then use a plain rasp at the end, and if the tooth is too sharp and wounds the tongue, you should file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens/falls out.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, either from a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot chew food without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines without success, then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth on the thread, if there is one or more, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again up to the point where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the teeth free with pliers and align them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose one, and position them so as not to injure the tongue; and then leave them as tight as they can endure, and if they loosen or the wire breaks, then constrict them with another wire; if they remain in place, it will serve them for their entire lifetime, and this is the method for aligning two loose teeth and two healthy ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place as soon as possible, as we have said; and one should not meddle with it unless they are wise and skilled; and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the gap where it is needed, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains in place for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes there is a ligament underneath the tongue, which is natural and present at birth, or it can be due to an accidental closure of a wound; and the procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth, hold their head in your hands, and lift their tongue. Then cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its anchorage, and if there is any hardness or knot, which is due to a sudden wound, insert the hook and cut it widely. Be careful not to make the incision too deep, as there is an artery underneath. After you have done this, apply a swab of rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue. The patient should change the bandage every night, to prevent reattachment. If bleeding occurs, apply a mixture of vitriol, and if the wound does not heal, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose. Finally, treat the wound with other treatments until it heals completely.[INTUITIVE AI] The text describes a medical procedure for treating a ligament under the tongue that may be present since birth or caused by an accidental injury. The procedure involves cutting the ligament to release the tongue and prevent reattachment. The text advises to be careful not to cut too deep to avoid damaging the artery underneath. After the procedure, the wound should be treated with appropriate medical care until it heals completely.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of fussey color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining toward blenchor, and there is moisture, throw onion peel on it, and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to meet your work, put vitriol powder on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the leu easily and gently, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come within the throat growths called "godath," which are properly called "the two almonds." And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and of fussey color, then do not touch it at all with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it at all with iron, for fear of bleeding; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will divide it, or it will break open by itself; and if it is of white color and swollen, and the root is thin, then prepare the instrument to cover it, but first see whether the hard abscess has settled down and is calm. Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and let his head be in your lap, and have the servant open the mouth and take hold of it between his hands, and press the tongue down beneath all the instrument, so that it may be as follows; and let it be of silver or fine brass, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And press the tongue down beneath all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the onion peel and insert it into the almond, and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, so that it may be as follows, which resembles forceps; and yet the jaws are close together, and one presses against the other, and it is made of iron, either iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool available, take tongs instead, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and once you have tonged one of the almonds, tong the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, and vinegar, and strained, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water or the peels of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then heal it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them then as you would the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely one of small size; and it had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the passage that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like that for one or two days. And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two pieces through the two nostrils. I therefore acted quickly, and inserted a probe into one of them, then pulled it out and extracted a large amount of pus; then I did the same thing in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut off a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again and filled the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; then I pressed on it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it ceased to grow, and I left. And I do not know what God did with her after I left.
de l’uve	of the grape (from Latin "uvam") or eye (from Latin "oculus"), Old French used "ueil" for both, so "de l'uve" is ambiguous in this language and could mean either "of the grape" or "of the eye".
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».
