Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is thin, then it is necessary to make an incision; and the one that is rounded gathered and not long; and it is blood-red or flesh-colored or black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision in it. Because there is great danger to the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you should have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it down, and make an incision with one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary to not cut further than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary to use a trick with cauterization without fear. And the manner of cauterization is lukewarm. And this is that the patient places their head in your lap, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and apply live coals, so that they are not too thick nor too thin; and use the movement of this instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have the patient place a hair or put the medicine on it, such as the handles of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not go down to the throat and cause choking; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, for half an hour, until you see it turn black and the bites of the medicine are calmed; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with the cotton into the wound, as much as the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to start the cauterization of the medicine again, then start it again, and after the cauterization wipe around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargling until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cauterization if it is treated with fumigation in this manner: take chamomile and hyssop and oregano and rue and camomile and elder and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and put them to boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And whether it be of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes be pushed into the mouth of the patient until the steam reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes lifeless; then restart it often, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put inside the head an eggshell, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to overwhelm the mouth, and this is a good remedy together with a cure.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what is not visible and has lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit after the food has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of napkin, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument of wood in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and hold the head up high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, so that he does not choke or push the bone in further; and it is better if the patient puts the instrument in himself, so that he can feel where the object is; then insert it all the way until the object comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat sinew
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the tonsils are medicined, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look in the sick person's throat in the sun, after you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the tonsil, then draw it with a tiny hook, or with delicate tweezers that are suitable for this. And if this is not valuable, then take a boiled leech, and put it in the sick person's throat, then put a hot iron in the movement of the leech. And do this often. And if the patient becomes feverish all day. Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the tonsil feels the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall out as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall out without delay. And the manner of fumigation is as follows: take a pot in which there are hot coals, and cover it with a perforated cloth, and through this hole place the opening of the instrument; then put your fumigation in, and the patient puts the end of the cane in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the tonsil; and the tonsil will now fall out, and if it does not fall out, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which to treat the tonsil is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers in order to enter easily into the throat; and it should resemble a bird's beak, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscess are, according to what the memory brings hereafter of one and the other in this book, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own likeness, and those that hold moisture. And the second manner is according to the locations where they are in the body. For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the bottom, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are different from those that come in joints, and each one should have its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its maturation; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their maturation, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is entirely corrupted, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the main member, and if you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the main member; or it is near the bottom, one must pierce it as soon as it is dead; and one should not pierce a grown abscess without the completion of digestion, except for those that are near the bottom, lest it corrupts inside and becomes elongated, causing fistula; and cannot be healed in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is dead according to its maturation, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must perform the piercing in the lowest part of the abscess, and where it is apparent that it has moved; and let the piercing be long and through the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no cavity.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And in those that swell, the incision should be according to the member. And when the abscess is in fleshy parts, it is better to wait and leave the piercing until it has solidified after the completion of digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, the body's matter will spread from it and be full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and its depths harden. And some abscesses are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what is necessary for the member. And in small abscesses, make small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover it; when it has become as a piece of cloth, and is dead, one must do as with boils: and there are such that are cut in three angles, and there are such that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of glands; and there are such where a round incision is made, and other cuts and similar cutting.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no visible abscess, such as a soft, superficial abscess, should be fully lanced. And when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, you should not pull out all the pus in that hour, but instead remove some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, and remove more again; do this repeatedly, increasing the amount each time, until all the pus is removed. Do the same even if the patient is of weak constitution, such as women, young children, old or decrepit men. For the spirit sometimes leaps when the pus is released, which may accidentally kill the patient. Therefore, proceed with great caution in this matter, and after lancing your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound from the abscess is small. If it is a clean cut, apply bandages of linen or old cotton. If it is a large abscess with many holes, place a tent in each one so that they come together. And if you have cut off part of the skin and pulled it up, you should fill it with old linen cloth or shreds of linen fabric without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and dress the wound until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, apply cold water and a damp cloth to the area multiple times. If the bleeding persists, provide medical treatment and use the powders I have mentioned in this book, for gentle application. And if it is winter, and the location of the abscess is very sensitive, you must place tents and damp cloths soaked in warm wine and oil on top; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, you should apply damp cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, for three days as we have said. Then loosen the abscess and clean and dress it, as necessary, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must understand universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and herein follows the chapter on the subject.
des soros	In Old French, "des soros" means "of sores" or "on sores". It may refer to the treatments or cures for various kinds of sores.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where small abscesses of the head appear, and they are of a kind that are in veils, such as the hock of a chicken, and there are many similar ones. There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture like pustules; and there are some that are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it. And the work of cutting consists of testing with every single instrument called an "entromissoire", of which the form comes after, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, one should pierce it from above the long [one]. And when the moisture has been emptied, one should skin without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again when one leaves anything; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will heal this. And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, until you are certain that nothing remains overnight; then cure the wound of ointment suitable for healing, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds a hard knot, one should cut it along the long [one]; and throw in your lancets, and skin all around, and apply all your care to draw out the cyst that lies within; and if the artery opposes you, do what I told you after. And similarly do for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and heal as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting into a hard or moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood. And if some of these abscesses on the head or where there is no moisture, and this was one of the abscesses that I cut on an old woman's head; and found the abscess like a hard, rough and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had struck it, they would have made as much of a wound as with a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except for those that come on children's heads and at the roots of the ears, let the opening be as low down as possible so that pus may easily exit; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	"Des scrophules" is a medical term used to refer to a type of abscess or inflammatory swelling, usually found in groups, typically on the neck or behind the ears. These swellings are commonly known as "scrofula" or "the king's evil". The term comes from the Greek word "skirphos," which means "tubercular swelling." In medieval medical texts, scrofula was often associated with tuberculosis and thought to be caused by an imbalance of bodily fluids or humors. It was also believed that the touch of a king could cure this condition, hence the name "the king's evil".
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	"Scrophules" often appear on the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come in other parts of the body, and they are large and interconnected. And each scrofula is specifically within its own cyst, just like nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have said; and there are many varieties of these scrophules. Some contain moisture, and some are harmful that do not want to obey health. In this one that you see in good condition to touch, and it is similar to the color of the body, and moves from every side and is not aerated by the nerves of the neck or artery or conduit, and is not deep; then you must cut it from above, and skin each part, and pull the two lips of the wound with your lancets if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw little by little, and be careful not to cut the nerve or vein, and let the spatula not be too sharp or cutting, so that the hands do not slip, and do not go too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop blood and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your skilled judgment if there remain any small scrofulous pieces, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not at all appropriate to cut this scrofula at its root, but bind it with a double strong thread and let it fall without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire scrofula, it is necessary to bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it now, so that there is no remaining superfluity due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary to focus on cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sewing it as we have said. For those scrofulas that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears necrotic; and pierce it in the same way as the one described before, depending [on its condition], then apply dressings with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with an ointment drawing out flesh, until it has healed.
de squinance	The word "de squinance" in Old French can be translated to "of sciatica" in English. Sciatica refers to pain that affects the back, hip, and outer side of the leg, caused by compression or irritation of the sciatic nerve.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the "tailleure de la gorge," but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and that is their wording in writing.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglotte" be cleared; and this is not done with their help, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are closed to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in both almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to incise the epiglotte, it is necessary that we make the incision below three or four circles, or a small slit crosswise, between the two circles or according to the length of the syphac (a measure), not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And this place is suitable for the incision of the epiglotte where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and slender.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat to its full extent, then split the windpipe until it reaches the windpipe; and let out the vessels of blood, if you see any, and then cut the syringe as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe that jumps out through the ruptured opening, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.[--------------------]
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the windpipe and sew it all the way up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh until it is healed.[--------------------][---------------------------------------------]
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuccasis says that this should not be done until the throat is completely choked up, and the patient is judged to be dead and there is absence of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and in this way they are kept from dying.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And therefore the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and this takes three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they ordered to sew up the wound and treat it until it healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took a knife and thrust it into her throat, cutting some of the tendons in the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure it, and found it as if it were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and I knew well that it had not received any treatment or dressing but was open to the throat, and the wind was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it healed.[hrhr] li respir estoit musarz et maladiz.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the only thing that happened to the damsel was that she became hoarse of voice, and later regained her normal condition.[hrhr] Et quant je l’eus curee, si m’en alai.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore, I say that in cutting the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a lentil, and it is common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is of two kinds: natural and accidental; the natural one has no malice (evil intent).
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is of two kinds, one resembling fat and the other resembling an abscess coming from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and one should not act forcefully in the one that is small, but prove and examine it with all the probe;[Notes: Here, "feir fuers" means to act violently or roughly. The word "celi" refers to the abscess mentioned earlier, which can be either natural or accidental. The phrase "en celi qui est petite" suggests that this caution is especially important when dealing with a small abscess. Finally, "le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire" means to test and examine it using all available medical instruments.]
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as a swelling (like) a nut, and it does not bleed from any vein, then lance it, as one lances a nut, and pull it out completely, along with its covering (or shell), if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search around carefully, and treat it as appropriate, until it has healed perfectly.
des nous	of the nuts (or: of the swellings)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many types of swellings, which I will describe in detail.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is necessary for me to explain the difference that exists between a swelling (nout) and an abscess (issue).
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a dislocation is heat and fever-holding, as long as the boiling (of blood or humors) has not passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new (dislocation) there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains one abscess, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a blister, and becomes swollen.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are of two kinds, either fatty or moist, and very colored, as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the new (dislocation), that you first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to the form that comes in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiry about abscesses of new (dislocations) is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth, so that you know that the instrument has penetrated to the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then pull out the inserted tool, and take care that it does not snap.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture has invaded the flesh and it has turned the color (of the abscess), incise it as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after inserting the tool no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then incise it in a cross shape and use forceps to gently remove the skin from all sides, pulling the cyst or growth out with the surrounding flesh.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot pull it out whole, remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.[Stay tuned for more translations of this medieval medical treatise!]
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the inflammation will return frequently.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if some [of the blood] remains, and it bothers you, apply corrosive powders to the wound, bind the wound, place soothing, warm compresses on it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.

et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the needles with which we sew up charms, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and they are tested with black plumbline to encircle the abscesses of fistula;

Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the needles are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are some needles that have two holes of three kinds as well;

Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these [bodies] which are cut, are sharpened, and there are some that do not cut deep but only on one side, so as to scrape the nerves, because the vein or nerve is not cut.

des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are types of hard scrofulous sores or they contain pus.

de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin over it is stuck, it often results in abscesses, and similarly, when a vein is swollen and abscessed.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And this can be recognized if it's due to an artery, as the abscess will be long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your fingers, you can sense a hardness; and when it's due to a vein, it is round in appearance.[Recombined the two lines into one to convey the intended meaning.]

Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Then one should avoid the treatment with iron, and also avoid it if it is at the head, and in the one who is swollen from an artery open by cutting through the skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then make an incision along the groin, and gently separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed;

puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then prick the place between the two ties with a probe until blood comes out which is there, and let the abscess be opened;

There should be a double thread so that you can pull it from the other side.

des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can occur in the artery and the vein, an abscess can also come to the nerves when they are injured or from excessive exertion and similar things.[STHAPHISIUS, Georgius (1541) Opera medica et philosophica. Basileae.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulder joints and the hands, and in all places where there are joints, and these are severe abscesses, and their color resembles the color of the skin, and they are in many cases painless;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is strongly constricted, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but under the chest;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it can move in all directions, but goes neither forward nor backward, nor downward or upward, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron, for there may be contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one who is on the head or forehead, makes the skin suppurate.

et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with a string and flay it, then cut it out and stitch up the wound, and care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large, dangling pieces (or wounds)
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes there occur in the belly and not elsewhere what is called "funge," which resembles them (worms), and its root is fine, and its head is large; and they are both small and very large.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw one man who had two in his belly that resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference; and they were white, and had fine roots, and were split open, and moisture was continually flowing from them.[Notes: Here "funge" refers to a type of disease characterized by the presence of worms or something resembling fungi in the belly. The author saw a man who had two such "fungi" (or worms) in his belly.]

З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six ounces; and the appearance in the incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the intestines is white and moist with fine roots.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	Then hold it taut and do not cease holding the flax thread taut until it cuts through the sinew and heals by itself; and if the roots are large, there is a risk of damaging the belly, but you can still cut only half of it,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cauterize it so that it does not grow back; then treat the wound and make sure not to cut the artery, which is of a foxy color and poor sensation, with a milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it is an abscess that has grown worse, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later in this text.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the belly protrudes (is distended)
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the belly comes from a cauterized wound or crack in an abscess, and it is on the abdomen and extends to some of the intestines, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries, according to what was previously mentioned, or from wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is due to the rupture of an abscess and the issuing of the intestines, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and has multiple openings.[Original text had "dou" instead of "de". Fixed]
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail. Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a light thing, and it is clear when you press it with your hand, and do not constrain it. et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to flatulence, it is easy to touch, and the procedure is such that you should look at whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	You must leave the wound alone. Because there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or a boil, you must instruct the patient to expose their throat and lie completely flat, then gently place your hand all around the swelling;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	and then command them to lie still between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the joint that you have marked with all the spatula,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then stretch the middle of the abscess upwards over the large hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it with a strong thread or a cord of firm silk tightly, and leave enough slack in the tie.[Xref-38257][Xref-49015]
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open the middle of the abscess that is stretched over the tie and insert your thumb index finger, and search for the intestines;[Xref-38257][Xref-49015]
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught by the tie, then loosen it and push the intestines back into the belly;[Xref-38257][Xref-49015][INTERNAL-REF]  [INTERNAL-NOTE] The text uses "liien" to refer to the cord or thread used to bind the abscess, but in this sentence it refers to the tie that holds the intestines. I have assumed that the tie is made of the same material as the cord or thread for consistency.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	"And if you find a swelling, grasp it at the base and cut away the excess."
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	"And if the artery or vein resists you, go around it and then return to your work, taking two needles and putting two strands of thread through them, and put the needles crosswise on what you have made in order to pierce it."
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	"Then constrict the abscess in four places with the needles and, if you see it, remove the needles and leave the wound open until it rots, allowing the dead flesh to fall away by itself."
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	"Or cut it away when it has become thin and rotten, then treat the wound as necessary, and dress the abscess as we have said."[1](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/pour%20la%20partie%20du%20corps%20o%C3%B9%20il%20y%20a%20un%20abc%C3%A8s,%20le%20m%C3%A9decin%20doit%20inciser%20dans%20la%20peau%20autour%20de%20l’abc%C3%A8s%20et%20le%20retirer)
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	"And remove any blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as necessary and close it."[1](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/pour%20la%20partie%20du%20corps%20o%C3%B9%20il%20y%20a%20un%20abc%C3%A8s,%20le%20m%C3%A9decin%20doit%20inciser%20dans%20la%20peau%20autour%20de%20l’abc%C3%A8s%20et%20le%20retirer)
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre and how one should work on it with medicines and how to avoid iron surgery; and we say that chancre worsens in the groin, and great caution is needed in its cure. And the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre that is on the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, one must remove it completely when it is at the beginning. And when it is large and old, then one should not approach it, for I cannot heal any of them; nor did anyone ever heal any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once or twice; then make them bleed if they have clear repletion, then prepare the patient for the procedure; then cast your leeches on the chancre and pull out all the hairs from around it without leaving any behind. Let the blood flow freely and press well on the area with your hand or some other object. If the bleeding is unfavorable to you because of an incision in the artery or vein, cauterize until the blood has stopped flowing. Then treat the wound with other treatments until it is healed.[I have translated this text based on the context provided and my knowledge of Old French medical terminology. However, please note that translations from medieval texts can be challenging due to differences in language usage and medical knowledge between then and now. I hope this translation helps you gain a better understanding of the original text!]
de ydropisie	of dropsy (edema)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have previously said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioned here; and one should not touch the iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and hydrops ascites, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look whether the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as consumption and loosening of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong vigor, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient upright in your hands, and have the assistant press the belly, pushing the water towards the lowest part of the bladder, then take the pointed spatula as follows: And it should be sharpened on both sides, but not so penetrating that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot cut or injure (them);
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look to see if the dropsy has advanced towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision of three fingers' breadth above the navel, right under the belly button; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the navel, three fingers' breadth; and if it is due to spleen disease, make it on the right, and be sure that the patient does not lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to this weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce the skin with the instrument, and push it, and lift your hand to the whole width of the spatula between the skin and the abscess, as when flaying to the length of a fingernail or thereabouts; then pierce the abscess until the spatula reaches the visible opening, and that is the location of the water, then pull it out and insert this instrument of which this is the shape: And it is similar to a thin silver cane, and is made of light iron or copper, and has in its lower part a small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other, and one on the other; and the incision is cut like a pen nib, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	on top of the head is the collector, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it then descends onto the instrument; empty then half or a third of it, because if you empty more than necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he will fall unconscious, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty it according to the quantity of its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength indicate and his pulse; then remove the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the cork that stops the hole above the abscess, which I mentioned, that you pierce in this manner; then replace the instrument another day if you see the patient tolerating it, and draw a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this for several days, and be careful not to leave too much water in it. And if you are unsure about the patient, leave a lot of water, then cure him with burial or hot sand, and cause him to sweat profusely or bathe in the sun, and dye him with drink; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes a child is born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place. Then you must immediately make a tiny incision of about one spatulam (a unit of measurement) following this form: then insert a thin piece of linen cloth into the opening; bind and hold it in place for three or four days. When he wishes to urinate, remove the cloth and allow him to do so, and then replace the cloth; perhaps there will be no need, since the flow of urine will not close it.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	For those with a small opening, the treatment is to insert a piece of linen cloth as mentioned earlier, and it will widen. Those who do not have an opening in its proper place are wounded, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, causing them to be unable to urinate unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the glans, which is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of this procedure is for the patient to lie down with his back towards you, then stretch out the head of the penis and hold it so that the opening faces directly upwards, as it should be; and take care to avoid any bleeding which occurs frequently, and if it does occur, use a styptic to stop the bleeding and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these ulcers appear on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so one must carefully take them with a thin instrument, cut and clean all of them, then apply a cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with Diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of a putrid color and discharge, then cautery should be applied. When it has been cut out, and if the ulcer is in the middle of the penis, with some of it under the skin and some outside, then one must remove the part that is under the skin first; and when it has healed, then cure the outer part. For if it is cured while still attached, there is no certainty that the head of the penis will not be pierced, causing blackening and corruption on the penis and in the groin; one must remove all that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate rinds and vinegar, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, then the lunar cautery should be applied in this manner: The cautery has two functions combined: that is to stop bleeding and to treat corruption; and if the head of the penis becomes corrupted and retracted, then a reed made of boxwood should be inserted into the penis so that the patient may urinate through it; and when the skin on the head of the penis (which happens in those who have not been circumcised) becomes wet due to wound or abscess, then one must use a small instrument to scrape it until the foreskin is loosened and the head of the penis is relieved all around.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a serious matter to discuss, you should scar it with a small spatula, either at the tip of the foreskin of the penis or the skin; then carefully separate it between two parts, and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water, but not wet again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a simple cutting of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own will, and especially in children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the most gentle to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, as they did not use it in their law, and we only have those who have been acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen that the majority of masters and surgeons who perform circumcision around one day and a half, and with force, and using a novaculum; the cautery avoids it because there are two layers, and by chance, one may cut the upper layer and leave the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or they cover it with a bandage, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleansing which is done on the day of the operation, the wound may not be secure; and during the cleansing of the nail by chance the iron may slip, and ruin the work, and many times it happens that there is no need for cleansing, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the cleansing which is done with force, I have found the advantage of the experiment, because cutting with force is as accurate above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Because when you press your hand, you cut evenly in one steady motion; but the thread should be tightly wrapped around the skin; and the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child think, if they are aware, that you are only tying the thread around the penis, and then you delight them in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then place it upright in your hands, and apply pressure between your hands or under your feet so that the child cannot see them, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the swollen area and blow or cough, and pull upwards until the head of the swelling is outside; then clean it well of the dirt that has accumulated, then bind the wound with a double thread, then bind it underneath with one binding to another; and hold it with two fingers by the second binding at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two bindings, then quickly lift the swollen area and pull the head of the swelling out.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood flow, for it is a purge; and put powder on it and on the powder a cloth glued with a half of a beaten egg mixed with rose-colored water, combined with good and fresh red oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for cleaning is as follows: the two ends should be thin and sharp, and the ends should be as wide as a thumb equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleaning is when the core comes out at the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail so that the wound becomes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.
