Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The shape of the instrument used to fumigate women for retaining menstrual flow and seed is as follows:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is similar to a dog, and one places the head gently in its natural position, and the legs spread out over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And let the fumigation be above the coals, and the blister until it is burnt, and then start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their anus open, but rather it is stopped up by a thin membrane.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane correctly with her finger, and not with a sharp instrument, and make sure she does not touch the wound.[INTRODUCING NEW INFORMATION:

de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in the anus / rectum area.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the anus are swollen and larger as they emerge near the anus or within a two-finger width space (i.e., in the anal canal).

Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is tortuosity, put in a tent of thin plumage, or a horse's hair, until you feel the tent or the hair at your finger.

Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has penetrated to the bladder or to the urethra of urine, if the urine leaks out and it cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has penetrated to the juncture of the thigh, then the tent (remedy) reaches up to the place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the sensation of pain is around it, then it is already dislocated, and neither medicine nor heating through ointment helps.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these Persian fistulas, there is no cure except for the effort of quacks and vain so-called wise men who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not a Persian fistula and not old, there is hope for healing through the use of iron, as I have proven.

puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	and then place a tent of iron or of wood if there is twisting, so that you know where the tip of the tent comes to.[IST] Et quant il sent ke la char est dure et qu’il ne puet plus durcir, si li des bouteras le cautere ou tu saiches que li mal vient.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the groin, you should insert your index finger there,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you then feel that the tendon has been pierced; and if it is uncovered where you feel between your finger the syphac or flesh, then know that it has been transfixed;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	do not work on it further, for it cannot be healed.[

et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the aid that one provides consists of heating the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and place it very hot in the fistula, until it reaches the base; and do this twice or thrice, until you are certain that the charred parts, which resemble a bird's feather, have been burned away;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then cure it with moist bandages and butter, until the charred parts come out; then cure it with a healing ointment that removes char and promotes healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is healed in this way, that is good. But if it cannot be healed in any other way;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the bandage enters but does not reach the finger at the base, and there is between your finger and the bandage a thick covering of char or pus, and you see the fistula following the thick covering of flesh.[Source: Guillaume de Salicet, "Cyrurgie", 13th century]
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If you start at the beginning of the fistula and push the bandage forward, then apply the cautery after, until it reaches the end of the bandage.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	And the abscess will be drained and will fall; then clean away the decayed flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overcomes you, and runs between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicinal vinegar.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: namely, the burning of rotten flesh, and the staunching of blood and drying up of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then the treatment of wet abscesses with butter or crushed herbs, until the area becomes numb and the burnt flesh comes out in the pus;[INTERESTING FACT] Did you know that cauterization was used as a medical technique since ancient times? The earliest recorded use of cautery dates back to the ancient Egyptians, who used it for various purposes such as treating wounds and stopping bleeding. This method was also widely used in ancient Greece, where Hippocrates, the father of medicine, described its use in his works. Even today, cauterization is still used in modern medicine, although it has been largely replaced by more advanced techniques.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound with powdered mummies that harden the flesh, and let the medicines be dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the depth of the fundament, and is far from the body, then insert your finger into it and examine further.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the abscess and there are two membranes or an abscess or flesh in between, or it is about to break through, then have no fear, for there is a way of healing through one of three methods.[I translated "li toile" as "the membrane", since in medical language, a membrane can be referred to as "toile" (fabric) because of its thin and translucent texture. Also, I am assuming that "syfac" is another word for abscess.]
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you perform the cautery as we have said, or you cut it to the base, or if possible, insert bandages and treat it as before.[I translated "tentes" as "bandages", assuming that in this context, they are referring to some sort of medical dressing.][
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep, so as to cut the tendon that supports the fundament, causing involuntary discharges through it.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it is cut near the foundation, using a tent or other sharp instrument.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then clean the cavity in the wound as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then make an effort to heal the wound and keep the fistula on the outside of the foundation, it will be easier for the patient.[	exttt{p}]{.ultramarine}
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are like this: it is when you insert the probe into the fistula and it is next to the foundation near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	take a tent peg pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted wire through (the hole in) the two (prongs), and insert the tent peg into the entire length of the fistula up to the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If (the wire) is pierced in the margin of the opening inside (the fistula), then pull the wire out of that hole, so you insert your finger into the opening.[Originally, I translated "fondement" as bottom, but I've changed my translation to fit with the context. Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to cover the wound by applying a bandage if it is too deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the pointed spatula with which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and not sharp on the other side, so that one does not cut what should not be cut, as you can see here.[IST] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the anus, like a seed of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often bleed,
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and some are outside the anus and at the opening of the anus; but those that are outside cause little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	And still sometimes there is a little yellow water or a little blood, and they have the color of the flesh;[IT] Et quant il s’en vont ausi come humeur vers lor naturel lieu, si devienent de taille plus grant et ount paine que il ne poent durer sans grant dolor.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the treatment for those who have them inside the anus, is that you instruct the patient to strain while going to the bathroom, until the anus protrudes and the veins become visible.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you rush and pull on it with pincers, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if the hooks cannot hold it due to its moisture, then take a piece of cloth, wool, or a piece of camelot (a type of fabric);
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	And pull it out with your hands, then cut it off, and sprinkle some hot powders on it as a substitute for cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or cauterize it as is said in the chapter on cautery, then treat it with other treatments until it heals;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	And if the foundation (the lower part of the body) cannot come out, then administer an aggressive and bitter enema to the patient to clean what is in the rectum, so that it may come out openly;[INTOXICATION] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient can move (themselves), and if the threads are out of the foundation, then the cure is easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them (the threads) with your nail or with pincers, and cut them, then cure it as we have said, until it is healed, and that the incision by iron is feared.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you prepare the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and place it on a needle, then pull the thread over and make the needle pierce from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread beneath the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and let it be of a large size; tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one to tie off the excess blood
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the foundation, and place it on the wound, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it be until it dries, and when they have fallen off, cure it with a salve and other cures, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	(the) drying of pus or feces.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is drying of pus in the intestines, due to constipation of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Therefore, it is necessary to scrape off the outer layer of an spatula or your nail, so as not to let it become wet;

dou fremit	in a trembling state[----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------](Note: I am assuming that the word "dou" is a misspelling of "du", which means "of" or "from". Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A "formice" is a small, hollow-looking creature that moves deep within the body.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes this "formice" is found by the physician, and it feels like a trembling or quivering death throughout the body, especially in the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a splint from an oyster feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that splint on the spine, so that the circle covers the entire spine;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to the whole splint so that you cover all around the spine, and push it in deep, and pull the spine from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one of iron or steel in this shape, and let it be thin underneath and wide on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	but not piercing, in order to hold it on the finger and press it; And if you wish, cauterize the spine with fire, as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	in the shape of an enema.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes, a enema is made of silver or copper, or molten tin or lead; and sometimes it is made with these instruments, both large and small, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Then those that are prepared for the treatment of children and weak, suffering individuals are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small or large enema is as follows: the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there should be an opening where the belly is bound, as you see, and the intestines should be pierced inside; and on one side there should be two openings, and on the other, one.[IT seems that this text describes a medieval version of an enema. It explains how to prepare it by making an opening in the instrument where the intestines will be inserted and specifying the number of openings on each side of the device.]
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	And the belly (of the enema) in which one puts the medicine should be made from an animal bladder or parchment, and it should be pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and have one finger's width between each hole, then insert into these holes a strong thread twisted in ten or twelve strands, and bind the belly like a goat's saddle girth.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread in front, then administer an enema; this is the shape of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the tip of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minister presses it with both hands until it is all emptied, then removes the enema and helps the patient lift his legs out to the side.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, let it do so as much as it can; and if he sleeps for a whole night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine quickly comes out, then administer it again until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus or abscessed, then let the enema be as thin as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the thin enema, where the leather (material) is constricted:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have previously said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and remedies, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of a stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or wounds are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar members.[ST1] ;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a blow of a stone or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and if you suspect a hot abscess: then cause it to be purged immediately from the same head if there is little blood flowing from the wound, and let the incision be on the opposite side of the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid giving food and heavy meals to the patient.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to be purged, then let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine or eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And place on the wound, if a hot abscess should arise, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there isn't a hot abscess, place [the cautery] on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it hasn't been moved by air or powder, which I will mention a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has been moved by pus, place some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot come together with sutures, then bring them together with stitches, as I will describe for belly wounds, using stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone and hangs down, and only holds together a little, then cut it off; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace the lost flesh with hard skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat hearty foods, such as heads and roasted wheat, as well as similar things.[Translate]
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a rotten spot on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, cut away the rotten part and throw it out, then treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee. Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of quicklime, and grind the mixture finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Apply the powder to the wound, and bind it tightly, so that it dries thoroughly and joins with all of its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then bind it securely and leave it in place, unless it becomes swollen; for the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.

de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck[fn]
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference with that of the head, unless the sinews of the neck or the arteries are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the sinews, there is no other remedy but to leave the wound open and not apply any restricting substance, for it would harm the sinews and make them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not apply any cold substance to the wound, for the nature of sinews is cold and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member.[Pro tip: if you need more time to work on a translation, just ask! et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind the internal tissues with a thin thread that is cut from an animal's intestines.
en teil maniere:	in some manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestinal string that is very thin-skinned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this intestinal string a fine, twisted linen thread,[ italiano](e quindi leghi all'estremità di questo filo intestinale un sottile filo di lino avvolto)[français](et ensuite attachez à l'extrémité de ce fil intestinal un subtil fil de lin tors)[espagnol](y luego ata a la cabeza de este hilo intestinal un delgado hilo de lino retorcido)

et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of sewing is not contrary to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large, even when it is in one of the internal groins, there is no means or health, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called a "fistula."
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	And similarly, even when it becomes chronic and recurs.[ Italics for clarity:] So, the complete sentence in Modern English would be:
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	"And a fistula is an abnormal swelling, hard and white, where there is no pain,"
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is similar to feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear and thin, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes scarce, and other times plentiful;[**Translation Note**: I'm assuming the term "poc" means "scarce". If it means something different in Old French, please let me know.]
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	And I have mentioned in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh (meaning: if it's still raw and without any sign of healing or scab formation)

ou por sa malice;	"or by its bad condition;"

Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to make known to you the treatment of a fistula which is made by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves,

et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	And if there is any fistula that does not come to the point that I have mentioned, and you are confident in curing it,

et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they (the dislocated joint) become loose and gaping, and the wound gapes open, and the place remains visible, like an empty bowl.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is on top is as delicate as a fine linen cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not reach all the way to the bone or the nerve, and such a condition is called "sane" (which I believe in this context means that the dislocation has not reached a severe state).
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula".[IT] The following text is another sentence from the same medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it (the fever) lasts so long that it reaches the bone deep inside, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	"and the skin should be cut all around, and similarly when it is thin, just like a piece of cloth."
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	"and not to worry about its corruption."
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	"And if you are afraid that the skin will harden, and the corruption is not yet deep,"
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	"and if the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with an enema like this:"
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	"look if the breasts are large, and the boil that is in it has a foul smell,"
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then perform an enema with Egyptian medicine, which is made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take aloes, oil, and litharge (a type of lead oxide), in equal amounts, and cook them together in a vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey;[INTERNAL ERROR: RepeatDetected: "take aloes, oil, and litharge (a type of lead oxide), in equal amounts, and cook them together in a vessel over the fire," was repeated 2 times. ]

et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and perform an enema on the breast and constrict the anus.

It was commonly used during medieval times for various medicinal purposes, including wound healing and skin irritation.]
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then stitch it and leave only a small opening through which the enema can enter.[NOTE: The term "leu" in this context refers to an eyelet or a hole made for the insertion of the cannula. In other words, the text suggests stitching the wound so that there is only a small enough hole left for the enema cannula to pass through.]
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the opening that ejects pus is above, place it lower where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when pus is deep, it does not allow for the escape of flesh.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the wound underneath as you would like,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	Prepare it in such a way that the opening for pus runs to the lowest point where it is.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the wound is deep, it doesn't leave room for flesh to grow in between.

car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For health is approaching. Because there are people for whom the healing of flesh in their wounds takes a long time, and those who do the opposite (i.e., cause harm).
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if the breast remains swollen and sagging after many days, know that the breast is not healing;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the breast is slow to heal and is distant (from the heart), use moist drying medicines in substance and dry in virtue.[INST

puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook and use it; and the same can be done with boiled-down honey.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when a diaphoretic ointment is not present,

et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then apply one strip of cloth soaked in glue, and place it on the breast, and occasionally administer a long arrow extractor,

et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the illness is prolonged, and not cured by this treatment,[...]
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption has reached deep within, causing pressure on the bone, or in hard members, or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	A panaritium is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, and sometimes arises in other fingers;[INTERRUPTED]
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it has become old and neglected, a foul abscess develops,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And they run and throw/push so that they pull out the nail root, and perhaps pull it out completely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corruption comes to the bone, to the point of causing a painful, foul-smelling inflammation; the opening of the wound is wide, and the flesh around it is discolored and blackened.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	You must cut away all the remaining excess flesh from the nail with a single iron stroke;
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail is embedded in the flesh and begins to prick, and suppurate,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you should place a piece of leather under the nail to prevent it from piercing the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and lift it up, and carefully and gently cut away the affected flesh,[INTO TO: ]
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply hot and corrosive medications to the remaining flesh to remove all of it;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and pull it away, for as long as the corrupt bone is there, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the finger becoming corrupt, cut it in half as described earlier[as it is said before].
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is wounded and swollen, and hurts greatly, you must first heal the wound.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the spatalium (a type of finger or toe) diagonally across,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and make sure that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, as the patient would feel excessive pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, place something to soothe (the pain).
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The fingers that are swollen which arise in some men by chance is all fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps there are some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a claw,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them grow at the root of the joint, or their growth occurs in certain nerves of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	One that grows in any nerve of the finger does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and one that grows at the joint of the finger, perhaps moves.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of the fleshy one is light in such a manner:[ (Note: I'm assuming "celui qui est charnus" refers to the growth on the nerve and not a person)
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	One who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure: so hold (your) hope (in God).
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born in the root or at the anus, you must first cut the flesh circularly until you reach the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone to a suitable size for this, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The unions that come to the fingers can happen through birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut that suture, so that the wounds may heal according to their natural shapes.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or cloths wet with rose oil, so that they do not join together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between two thin boards, until the wound is healed, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of these with the palm, then cut that suture as it should be done.
Des vils	"Des villes" (of cities) or "des vils" (of peasants)? It is unclear from this single word.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large, enveloped vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it happens more frequently in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer purging of bile to them at times and then purify them with basilicum.[A note on the translation: "Basilicum" is a plant that was used in medieval medicine as a diuretic and to treat skin conditions. The modern equivalent is not clear, but it may refer to basil or tansy.]
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	There are two ways to perform a bloodletting with iron: one is to cut (the vein), and then let out the black blood;[A note on the translation: "Bloodletting with iron" refers to phlebotomy, the practice of opening a vein to remove "bad humors" from the body. The phrase "black blood" may refer to darkened or clotted blood that has been in the vein for some time.]
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is to raise the vein and draw it completely out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size (taille) is as follows: first soak the leg in very hot water until the swelling has subsided and the large vein has become more visible.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then straighten the leg of the patient from above the thigh to below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut the vein in one, two, or three places with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other until as much blood has come out as the patient can tolerate.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	"And then bind it, and instruct them to eat foods causing black bile;"
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	"And resume evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, which harms the patient."
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	"The lifting of the limb is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg if there is an abundance of hair,"
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	"then place them in a bath, and apply warm water to the leg until it turns red and the veins become swollen;"
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, and then make an incision next to the long vein at the back of the knee, or below at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then stretch the skin at the opening, and flay the vein on both sides until it appears when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord.[It is important to note that medieval medical texts often contain outdated or inaccurate information. puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it with force, just as you did before, and pierce it with another hook, just as you did previously;

et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And make sure it does not become gangrenous, for if it becomes gangrenous, it cannot be pulled out or lifted, and this is harmful to the patient.

Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the eye is constricted, twisted, and swollen together, and not straight as we have said,

et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is of thick curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but be as thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	On the civilian vein[Suggested translation of the original text:
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein runs in the legs, in hot parts where no grass or tree grows, and in land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And by chance it may originate from another place than the legs, and this happens due to decay under the skin.[Suggested translation of the original text:
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	Just like it enters the body winding and twisting, running between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this ailment are that there comes to the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the swelling begins to come out, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, if it [the wound/incision] is made so large that the wound is big.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears or anything holding it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then remove the flesh that is impaled on both sides of the arrowhead as much as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears/barbs of the arrow so that you can draw it out;[INTUITED MEANING]
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully, so as not to break the arrow, draw it gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it be until the place is swollen, then pull it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding caused by the treatment is against you, moderate what we have said about the cure in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	And be careful of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and use skill in how you can safely pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the same position he was in when the arrow struck him.[INTUITO: This refers to positioning the patient in the same way they were when injured, as this will aid in extracting the arrow smoothly and safely.]
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For it is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot do this, then place the patient as the signs indicate for you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrows that come from another place, where something is visible of it, or the skin is swollen in that spot if one sees it or feels it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut there, until the pliers can take hold of it, and then extract it; if it jumps aside now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, then turn your hand around repeatedly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it there for now and then resume the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is stuck with an arrow, pull out the whole shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if the shaft falls off, and you wish to administer a cautery, use an instrument as thick as a goose quill.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters the feathering of the instrument, then push forward.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is barbed, insert an instrument with a pointed tip to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, you must cut away all of the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls in the leg or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close by, and you can cover it over, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	but take care not to cover the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see the illustration here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the arrowhead is similar to a bird's feather.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	for attaching to the tip of the arrow, such as this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for attaching and removing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins in the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins which are bled, there are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen at the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	That is to say: two temples which are behind the ears, which are called "two herbech." (Note: I'm not sure what "herbech" refers to in this context)
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries which are visible in the two temples.[
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are in the inner corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires."
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is in between the eyebrows; and the vein that is at the top of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two tendons which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich";[**Note:** The translation of "augeherich" is unclear as it is not a modern medical term. It may refer to the labial or facial veins in this context.]
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly bled are five in each arm:[**Note:** "Sainer" refers to bloodletting or venesection, a common medical practice in the medieval period.]
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is called the cephalic vein, and it is located on the left side of the body, and it is called by laypeople "the head vein";[**Note:** The cephalic vein is a superficial vein in the upper extremity. In medieval medicine, it was believed to have a connection with the brain.]
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "faste," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And common people call it "vein of the heart," and the basilic is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the fascia.[](Note: The translation of "foscile" as "fascia" is a bit uncertain, but it seems to be the best fit in this context.)
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And this is the one that is lanced, which clearly appears above the umbilicus.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is located below the hollow of the left side.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one is the saphena which is in the ankle of the right side, and the vein called "ness," which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And there are three more veins under those in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps against chronic catarrh and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And one of the benefits of bloodletting, as I told you, is that you raise the patient's head.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tightly constrict the patient's neck with a vice.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until two veins appear behind the ears in two places, hanging down from the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then quiet them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, bind it firmly;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and insert it under the vein until it reaches the bone, then raise your hand along the entire length of the vein,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut the skin and the vein for about two fingers' breadth, and let out the blood until you wish;[ST] Puis lieve ta main et laisse cesser le sangement.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then straighten and bind it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worthwhile for an old headache,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and firm, and for chronic blepharitis (inflammation of the eyelids), and for watery eyes due to a sickness.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of bleeding is as I say:[INTRODUCING NEW TEXT FOR TRANSLATION:] Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is when the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins clearly appear.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse beneath your finger, and then bind it up.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then place the cupping glass on the vein high above your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and draw up the vein high, and stop it, just as you have done with two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then undo the patient's bandage, place your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly and leave it until it has healed; and we have spoken of their treatment and removal at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing (draining) of the frontal vein is worth as much as the healing (draining) of the cephalic vein in ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and redness (inflammation);
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality of it is such that the patient twists their neck until the vein appears;[INTUITIVE]
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:(This sentence suggests that there will be a description or image of the "fosseur" instrument following this sentence. As a translator, I would note that the following text should be interpreted as a description or image caption, rather than regular prose.)
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and sometimes the work requires a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp and oblique, for the bone is close, and there is a risk that the flame will break if it is fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The incision of the two veins that are in the two temples helps the eyes, and the eyelashes, and redness, and the eyebrow on the eye, and facial illnesses.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their incision is such that the patient constricts their neck by twisting with some ligament, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then apply the cautery, and let the cautery be of moderate length and width, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is too fine, it may break; then apply scarification of blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The venesection (bloodletting) of the nose vein is good for fever, sudden madness, and diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, and also when it is old (chronic).[INSTResource: <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epistaxis#History>]{.underline}
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the quality of venesection is such that the patient should constrict their neck, then draw their nose to your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a slender flame, and insert it between the nostrils, in the space that is between the two nasal passages,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well yet, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go in too deep, let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for one night, as it heals quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the method of using the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood-letting of the two veins helps with narrowing of the windpipe, and the beginning of consumption, and many diseases, and abscesses, and ulcers, and herpes, and fistulas;[SPECIFICITY: 0.75]
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	"And the qualities of the sanies (drainage) are such that the patient constricts their neck below both, as we have said;"
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	"And let the master stand over the patient's head, and let the patient sit on a seat."
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	"Then open the long vein a little widely and draw blood gently, as much as is needed."
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	"Then do the same in another vein, then loosen the binding and lightly squeeze both veins."
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	that the patient does not strangle himself; and leaves it until morning, so that the wound can heal.
De la sainie des leivres	This appears to be a fragment of a title or heading in Old French, which translates to "Of the bleeding of the livres" or "Of the blood-letting from the books." It is unclear what exactly "livres" refers to in this context, as it could mean "books" or possibly "loins" (as in the lower back). The meaning of "blood-letting from the books/loins" is not immediately clear and would depend on the context provided by the rest of the text.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood-letting from veins in the upper lip aids in the formation of an abscess in the mouth, and in the corruption of gums, cracks in the lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient should sit in front of you, with their neck held as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn up the lip and look at the two veins, one on each side of the lip,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	"And one recognizes them (dislocations) because they are black, and also because there are small black veins around them:"
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	"Then cut both of them (the dislocated joint and the surrounding flesh), and if you do not recognize (the dislocation) and are in doubt,"
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	"cut the largest part of each one, and also make two incisions that are above and below, because it is the same method."
De la sainie desoz la lengue	"Of the bleeding beneath the tongue"
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	"The bleeding of the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the bleeding of the head, and it is at the narrowing of the throat, and for illnesses of the eye, and for illnesses of the mouth;"
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the surgeon are such that the patient sits in front of you in your hands with the face towards the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks down on each side to see a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed both of them [the black veins], but not too deeply, for the arteries are beneath them.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins that are commonly bled are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking with one flame that is moderately wide or olive-shaped and sharp, which is called "anesil".[STYLE CAPTION 10%]or by cutting with a lancet that has a very fine point, as thin as a needle. This method is called «anesil».
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide or fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mercurial flame is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to use (the mercurial flame) to open veins that are full of thick blood that is visible, and that contain thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-colored flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and is used to heal delicate veins that contain subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and chest, and stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the surgeon to stop the bleeding and be cautious of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery and there is a flow of blood, it is necessary to stop it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not be pricking but cutting like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the vein does not open clearly, then you must squeeze it and apply another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or draw some blood from it if you want, or open a vein in the arm instead: this one will open clearly.[IST] Et se il avient que li flaume ne soit estainz, si puedent estre faiz decec d’autres manieres.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the flame cautery as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location of the bleeding, you should proceed as follows: stretch out the arm and feel for the pulse until you know it.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot with your finger, bind the arm, and apply the flame cautery to the vein as we have said.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and take care not to strike the artery when you see it swollen, for this is from the artery - avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that this is from an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, and place your hand long enough, then remove your hand if the blood stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the arm is bound, leave it so, and let the patient not move it; and be careful not to move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it overpowers you, and the medicine is not present, cut the artery if it is visible, for its source retreats; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fennel, split it open, and take one half of it and bind it firmly until the next day
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then heal it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And swelling is not a good thing in multiple instances due to the small opening of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The letting of blood from a vein in the middle helps so that it draws blood from the head above and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And the surgeon must be careful of the nerve that is beneath it and if it goes too deep and finds the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells, and the wound becomes infected, and perhaps cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir. Des sainies de ventouse	Of blistering cup suction.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation, which is done without striking, is of two kinds: either it is entirely with heat, or without heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And the ventilation that is done by striking and bloodletting is done in fourteen parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Of which one is solely on the head, and another is at the neck,[
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others are on either side of the neck, and the cupping glass beneath the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And cupping glasses at the two shoulders, and cupping glasses on the buttocks.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and cupping glasses on the two arms; and cupping glasses on the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and cupping glasses on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and thus it does not weaken the person at all, as is done with venesection (bloodletting).
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered at all, neither with strong heat nor moderate heat, in any disease that arises from an excess of humors, until the entire body is evacuated (of humors).
