Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are valuable for old pains in the shins, joints, bladder, and help with inflammation; they are placed near the two ankles and the two calves, yet despite this, they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is as follows: place it empty first, and then attach it quickly with gentle heat, moving it evenly, not stopping until you see the area turn red and swell, and observe the color of the blood that comes out; then pierce (the skin) and replace the cups, taking care of the condition of the body, for there are those who have dry and clear pores: so you should pierce only once, making large but not too deep wounds, and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw little by little, one striking is sufficient.

et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for the one who has thick and tough skin, and narrow pores, to anoint the areas for the cups with oil that is apertif and dissolvent.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in the summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucumber seed.[STT: In the summertime, use violet oil, sweet almond oil, or oil extracted from cucumber seeds.].

Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish surgeons throw themselves away from this chapter, for they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they ever read (them).[note] I added "them" to make the sentence grammatically correct in English. Therefore, it is appropriate that we mention in the prologue of this book the summary of the teachings and the chapters in which the wise person concentrates their understanding and dwells on the truth, so that those who are tested may know and learn this noble art, and then teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or bruise occurs in someone, you must quickly heal the patient from all sides if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of the body, infants, or the elderly;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is not extremely hot or very cold, and you feed them cool foods, such as cold meats like chicken and hare, and they do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill up on food that fills the veins with blood, until there is doubt about a hot abscess or spreading of matter to the limb; then the patient should return to their normal diet that they were used to.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when a broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote thick nutrition, such as wheat boiled in water, and bread, meat, poultry, dairy products, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For proper nourishment promotes movement and speeds up the healing of fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the elderly and infirm cannot heal or join together well according to their nature because of the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But it doesn't matter, apply a large tendon to the broken bone, which sticks and joins the limb together until it heals as it was before; and do not stop working on it, and therefore it is necessary to nourish it with hearty foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a skull fracture is different than a rib fracture or a leg fracture, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are some fractures that go obliquely, and others sharp-angled, like the quill of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with just a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each type there is its own instrument and proper tool in restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place.[INT (from a different user): I have been following this translation of the medieval medical treatise. et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the break of the bone is apparent by the twisted place, and it is clear to touch with the press of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twistiness or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but there may well be a twist, or fracture, or small break.[HW Correction] Here's the corrected translation:
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move it by hand, but apply the following medications and then bind it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that breaks which go up the arm, and are in two separate parts, must be set evenly so that pus does not form.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	"And if boils or abscesses come there, let it be left alone for some days, until the abscess has calmed down;"
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	"then align it evenly as you can easily and quickly, and know that the healing of this one will be easier than the healing of those with broken pieces; then bind it as is appropriate."
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	"And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it with two pieces of wood, whether it be the leg or foot, or use your hand if it's a small limb, or use two ropes, or one rope and your hand;"
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	"and place the limb in its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you align all the fragments in their places as well as you can. Be careful that your work does not cause harm or pain to the patient."
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	"and join the two ends of the bone according to the best shapes."
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it in the hand if it seems not to be well: so straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who make it hot abscess and contraction in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient so that they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, turning over, or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And make sure that the limb is secured so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels any pain, then it is not healed, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And make sure it is set straight, so that there is no crookedness when it is healed.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	"And the qualities of the broken member are as I tell you."
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and form."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	"For there are small members, such as arms and legs and the like: one should wrap them with soft and fine linen bandages;"
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	"and those that are large, such as hips and legs: one should wrap them with a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire large member and constrict it equally on all sides so that there is no swelling;"[ Renforcez le membre par dessous d’un drapel de laine fine et blanche et lié tres fort, si qu’il ne s’en faille nullement.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	"Then bind soft sponges around it three or four times depending on the member, and pull your hand slightly at all the bandage, then go above the break and tighten less so that the break is moved away slightly;"[ Puis liez de cendal fort, que li cendals soit entor le membre et la brisure, et il covient que le cendal soit legier a traire, si qu’il puist destreindre et estreindre selon ce que tu verras.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament bit by bit, until you have taken a large part of the healthy place, then take another ligament, and turn it around again on the broken leg;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break, and hold it moderately, not too tight or too loose, as we have said in the first section above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place linen wool or strips of cloth between the ligaments until they are even, then bind it all with a bandage on top, and then place your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something that reduces the abscess and is warm, which removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind it to your splints, and let them be half the width of a cane for bleeding, or from wood that arrows are made, or from palm branches, and let them be in this shape;[attachment=38415]shape.png[/attachment]
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the steel/metal bar that one places on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also be as long as it is needed for the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tighten (strain) on the steel bars as you did at the first suture, then bind/tie a suitable thread over it, just as you did in the first suture on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	(the) tighter (it is) after that, the less (it should be); and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;[SPACER]
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of fools who make their sutures with twisted linen cords, that is a great error, for the suture cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is not at all appropriate to have less than two fingers' breadth between each steel bar.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded at the sides by the corners after being tightened in a healthy place, place under them linen or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a break and the flesh is torn, I will tell you the cure next.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to constrict all broken limbs with bandages on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	Because when the limb is large, bandages should not be used unless after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your certainty of a hot abscess arising;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of ancient poultices to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists: it is made from flour that sticks to the mill walls, mixed with a generous amount of egg, and this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, should be used. This is the common method of the restorative poultice for breaking in various ways, and also for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of making a plaster to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take centaury and laudanum and elecampane and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each in the amount of ten drams; aloe and aloewood, each in the amount of five drams; and eight drams of licorice root; and grind them into a powder, and mix it with egg white; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and is beneficial to many.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of making a plaster for twists: take myrrh and mallow, each in the amount of ten drams; aloe and acacia, each in the amount of six drams; Armenian bole in the amount of ten drams, and grind well, and infuse with water or egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way of making a plaster for joints and bones that have become dislocated from their places, and to soothe the resulting pain, and for use in cutting bone or fractures: take new wool, and moisten it with vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the area. This plaster does not heal, but it is good for relieving heat from abscesses and alleviating pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of making a plaster to heal fractured bones: take dried fig leaves and the leaves of wild peppermint, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way of applying a plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess. Take root of coltsfoot, chamomile, violet flowers, bran flour, an equal amount of each; and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the limbs are heated, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another stronger way of applying a plaster, compared to the first one, when hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of coltsfoot, flax seeds, balm, melilot, self-heal, violet and chamomile flowers, an equal amount of each; and grind, and make into a paste with salt water or sweet water, or with wine, depending on the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place anything on the broken member for healing except a wax and oil cerate, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen thinks that one should place dry and somewhat warm things on the broken member for healing, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is useful for wound and pain: take houseleek and chopped off human hair or bird feathers, and add vсмоlive (a type of plant) and equal amount of grease, grind them, and make it into a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then unbind it a little afterwards, and make sure the patient does not feel any pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place; if so, do not unbind it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and unbind it, remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth, and a sea sponge, soaked in water, raise the limb, until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool, wet with water or rose oil, and bind it on a cushion, until you are sure that there is no fever.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and remove the pain, then gently resume the fine ligament, and a little emplaster, and do not constrict it as before; and delicately until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess is red, swollen, painful and has opened up completely, and you need emplaster and ligature, then reapply it as you did in the beginning.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if the limb does not improve with any of the treatments we have mentioned, do not release it before three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what is observed, until the break heals and the setting approaches the flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then bind it more tightly than before, and the flesh will fatten as I said earlier; and if you see that the place dries out more than necessary, know that healing cannot come.[ITP-TEMPLATE] And if an abscess is red, swollen, painful and has opened up completely, and you need emplaster and ligature, then reapply it as you did in the beginning.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	boil the joint in hot water each time you release it, every third day, and slightly loosen the ligament;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	through this work, therefore, the blood flow to the limb is cut off and it heals quickly what foolish surgeons do, who mistakenly restore the limb: this is bad, and it is a frightening procedure, and I see no other solution but to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the different types of fractures.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with various shapes, and distinct causes;[SRP\_LINE\_BREAK]
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures made by sword blows, and the collarbone separates the bone all the way to the growth plate beneath the bone, as a hatchet or stick does: this type of fracture is called "hatchet-like" (haichure).[SRP\_LINE\_BREAK]
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a deep bruise, or a stone chip, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that reaches the membrane beneath the bone, or above it, and this wound is either large or small.[Note: The membrane referred to here as "toile" could be the periosteum, a highly vascular tissue surrounding bones, or another type of membrane.]
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has penetrated into the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called this type of fracture "hairline".[Note: The term "capillary" in modern medical terminology refers to tiny blood vessels, but here it seems to refer to the thinness or delicacy of the wound or fracture.]
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is caused by being struck with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and it drives a piece of bone inward, and the area is rough like when blacksmiths hammer on cauldrons, and stones enter inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their heads, such as the bone of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, like splinters; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the swelling on them, and through inquiry using tentative examination, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top.[Note: The word "corrupt" here likely means "damaged" or "injured"]
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of a fracture is recognized by this: when the bone is exposed and one rubs against it, the fracture appears black.[Note: "Black" here likely refers to discoloration or bruising caused by the fracture]
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be cautious of the patient's condition, and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, fever, eyes turning out and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.

et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck and under the healthy pelvis, and under the patient's affected pelvis; and massage each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture properly, and you can clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the bandages loosen, tighten them again.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	And make the patient lie on their back, and place a small cushion under their pelvis when they sleep, to raise the affected shoulder; in this way, the fracture will be relieved of some of its weight through the alignment of the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless there is an unfortunate accident, for 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the poultice, if you see that it is necessary, and bind it up and leave it in place until healed; and it is healed in the longest in 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture/dislocation
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates in a large or small place, and it is not noticed until touched; then set it according to the type of fracture, and reset it according to its natural shape, in all ways possible; then put on the surface powder of flour with plenty of egg, and light cotton, and place a double cloth over it; then place a wide and thin plate over it, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate in any part of the shoulder, fill those hairs with linen cotton, so that the plate lies flat; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, making sure that the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it softens, tighten it again, and make sure the plate is in place if it has moved, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is completed, unbind it and be careful, for it is not an easy bone to put back in place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out in front and not under the skin, then saw through it (the bone), and remove it, and do what we have said for the fracture of the forearm to soothe the hot abscess.[Notes: I am assuming "apaiser aposteme chaut" means to treat a hot abscess, as it is mentioned before in the text. The word "oste" here probably means to saw off the protruding bone. ]
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the ankle. And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a lack of alignment, and they may vomit blood, and the fracture can be seen in the broken bone, and it is evident to others.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies down with their back on a cushion placed between their shoulders, then presses their shoulders and brings the ribs together using both hands, subtly aligning all parts of the bone as much as possible, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply poultices and bandages over the fracture, with a thin layer of salt or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, tying it securely to the broken bone so that it does not move; tie the knot around their back, pulling it tight, and check every hour to see if it needs to be loosened, due to infection or itching at the site, or pain or abscess, and act quickly by untying it, removing the poultice, addressing any issues that have arisen through appropriate treatments; then reapply the poultice, tying it securely until healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breakers of ribs do not come about except in thick areas after the back, and at the head within, and they do not bend outwards except because they are slippery; and one can feel this well upon examination at the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the setting (of a broken bone) is such that you make the break even, as it should be. And then apply an ointment and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is declining inwards, then the patient feels great pain and swelling, just like with pleurisy, because the bone points at the membrane; and there is sharp pain, and soon they vomit a large amount of blood, and this is of grave illness, and the old ones have applied much skill to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to push the break outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that boils/abscesses come to it, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then lance them (let the pus out).
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you have said that cupping glasses should be placed over the place to strongly draw out (suction), and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass might attract impurities to the place due to its weak constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you have said that one should cover the place with a cloth soaked in warm oil and then place bandages between the ribs to evenly hold it in place around the area; and then treat it with the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone pressing against the cloth, and there is doubt for the patient, then one must make an incision on the place of the broken rib, and place a dressing underneath to protect the wound; and then cut the bone and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and dress it with poultices until it heals. And if boils/abscesses come, then place cloths soaked in rose oil on the area, and place them on the place; and treat the area as one would for a boil, and let the patient lie on their side where the wound is, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break (fracture) of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a break occur in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and likewise for the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, pay attention if you see their hands softened, swollen, and numb, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that in many cases, this means they are mortally injured, but if they can move them and feel when they are squeezed and poked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if given treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, pay attention if their feet are weakened, and if the conditions present in their hands are also there, and on their back, a wind-like movement and involuntary excretions occur; and when it is placed on its stomach, involuntary excretions still occur. And when it is placed on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot. Know that this is mortal: do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these conditions do not arise, then the matter is more manageable.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should check if there is a hot abscess, and if there is, put roset oil or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then apply one of the soothing and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the part where they feel pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound; remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the large wound with a stitch, and treat it with a drawing ointment until it heals; and if the joint near the bone is broken, which is called "the hip joint," place your left hand's pouch on it, and use your right hand to push it into place as much as you can, then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, push it back into place, remove it, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the femur (thigh) bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the femur is broken, but if it does happen, only a slight swelling occurs at the end; and it becomes long, and inclines to one side, causing pain and lameness to the patient in that area, and swelling in the affected limb.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand on top, so that you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the head only, then make the break even, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it angles inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of that break is made clear to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then apply the ointment, then place a wooden or waxen star* on top, and hold the break steady so that it does not move; and apply medicine underneath the ribs, until they are aligned.[Yves57] *It is likely that "estele" here refers to some kind of medical device made of wood or wax. The meaning of this term in Old French is uncertain and could also refer to a type of bandage or splint.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come after it, do not touch it until the abscesses have calmed down, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is necessary, if there is no adverse accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the one that is between the neck and the shoulder blade, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored in one of two ways: one of which is to take a rod of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two bands and pull them up, and make the patient sit on a seat; then throw his dislocated arm over the rod, until it reaches the waist, and has in the middle a bow of the rod; then hang it from some heavy weight or have the minister stretch it down; then place the surgeon's hands equally around the break, until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one lays the patient on their back, and ties their hand to their neck, then commands two assistants, such that one holds what is above the break with their hands, and the other holds beneath all the way to one ligament, and each pulls apart in their direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then one assistant pulls a ligament below the break and above it, while each of the assistants pulls apart in their direction. And if the break is close to the shoulder joint, then one must place a middle ligament below the socket and another towards the ribcage, below the break; and similarly if the break is towards the ribcage, one must place a light ligament without strain so that the break is even above the socket and above the ribcage; then align the break as it should be and hold it in place, if no abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess does form, then do not hold it in place for more than 7 days and place a moist linen cloth soaked in rose oil on the affected area; wait until the abscess subsides. Then hold it in place, and the manner of holding it in place is that you apply a poultice to the break, then position the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and place the cloth, and hold it in place on the shoulder and on the arm so that the arm remains still, unless something prevents you, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you are unsure whether the bone has moved, then use a splint and place a wider and stronger splint over the break than the others, with a space of one finger between each splint, and let each splint be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on either side; then hold it in place over the splints as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter, more firmly and less so as you move away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have mentioned, at the time you reset the broken member, and you doubt there is a hot abscess, then leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the binding every three days, to see if itching, inflammation or discharge comes to the place, or if numbness cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight. Loosen it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not loosen it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion full of evenly spread wool beneath the affected area, and examine every hour of the day and night, to see if the shape of the broken member moves, or if the binding becomes too loose; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give them food as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is initially fine; and when they begin to recover, let the food be coarse. And it is customary for the affected area and leg to fully recover in forty days; and then one should loosen it and administer baths and medicines with ointments to straighten the place. And if the stricture is bad and embedded, then wait one day or two months before loosening it.
de la brisure du bras	Here's the translation of the text you provided, in relation to a broken arm:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small and is the one that follows the wrist; and the other is large, and it is the one that is beneath, towards the little finger; by chance, only the large foscile breaks, or the small one, and by chance, both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration and healing is easy; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult and more severe than when they are both broken together. If it is only the small bone that is broken, then it should be gently stretched and put in its place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone, then it must be strained more; and it should be stretched out on a cushion, and the little finger of the hand should be held higher than the others, and the small toes lower than the other toes, and the patient should be lying crosswise on it, with a cushion before him that is higher than he can bear. Then the assistants should extend the patient's arms below to his side, or to a strap, and one assistant at one side and another at the other. And then the physician puts it in its place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break is in pieces, then put each one in its place; and if there is any piece that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision above it and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of this in a separate chapter; so take care of it (referring to the treatment described in the previous chapter).
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration pustules occur, then put on a piece of linen cloth dipped in a mixture of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and carefully place another cloth over it, until the pustules have calmed down. Then remove the linen cloth and apply the plaster made of powder from the mill with plenty of egg, then put on the stylets, and let the one from the breakage be stronger and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have six stylets or branches in multiple arrangements: either the breakage be in one of the bones, or in two; and bind more above the breakage than any other part, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are above the breakage be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread from which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And wrap the member and the bandage after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some misfortune befalls the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you must sprinkle warm water on the member until the itching has calmed down; and let the member not rest tightly. And then begin binding again, and if the bandages are weakened and the bones have separated, and similar things, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the circulation cannot reach the member because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it like that for several days, until the circulation has returned, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things that we have mentioned happen to the patient, then do not unbind it for twenty days or so; and in the meantime, let him keep his hands on his neck, with his collars even, and beware of movement and rubbing, and let him sleep on his back. And know that this breakage is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps even in twenty days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles often occur, but these are usually not true breaks, rather they result in frequent swelling.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or dislocated, it is necessary that the patient sits cross-legged and faces directly ahead evenly; then they place their hand on a spread out cloth, and the assistant straightens the broken bones and aligns them properly until they are joined; and then an ointment and bandages are applied, unless abscesses appear; then an iron bar is placed according to the size of the injury; and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.[EnglishGlossary.com](https://www.englishglossary.com) provides English definitions for many Old French words found in this text, including: * au (at, to), croisiet (cross-legged), devant (in front of, before), igalement (evenly), met (put, place), ministres (assistant, servant), os (bones), brisiez (broken), igalz (equal, even), joint (joined), envoloupee (wrapped), drapeil (cloth).* saiches (know), dos (back), poc (there is/are, have), avient (occur), maintes (many), ploieure (swelling), n’i (there not), mais (but, except), quant (when), estendue (spread out), puis (then), sovant (often), apres (afterwards), mal (badly, ill), briseures (breaks).* saiettes (arrows), ovrer (work), incision (incision), sus (on), aposteme (abscess), cure (healing), plaies (wounds), estraction (extraction), piere (stone), semblans (similar, like), doutance (doubt), paor (fear), mors (deaths), en vient (come), plusors (many).* quant (when), desaloiez (dislocated), cause (because), moistor (moisture), remet (set back), leu (place), ne peut demorer (cannot stay in place), revient (returns, dislocates), petit movement (slight movement), ades (repeatedly), avient (happen), ramoinnes (reset).* issue (occurs), jointe (joint), de son leu (from its place), por coi (because of which), ne se puet muevre (cannot move), mal figurez (misaligned), grant dolor (great pain), grant lesion (great injury).
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the outside around the stomach of the palm, make a sphere from a cloth and instruct the patient to squeeze it with their broken hand; then bind it with a long cloth, and let the iron bar be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is protruding, one should place a stick on top, and another underneath in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it entirely around the hand, and staunch the wound between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is in any of the fingers, if it's a simple one, place it evenly as it should be; and hold it with the palm, and if necessary, put a small straight stick to raise the fracture and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or another one, place it evenly and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together, whichever works best, or put a stick on top, like a splint; and be cautious during the restoration and placement of hot abscess, and treat accordingly, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Here's the translation of "de la cuixe brisie" from Old French to English:
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and it's easily noticeable when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists of tying one bandage above the fracture, and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant stretches out their rope evenly on their side; and that is when the fracture is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the thigh root, let one of the ropes be towards the wrist, and the other ropes below the fracture. And similarly if it is near the knee, and then let the rope be next to the knee, and the extension downwards; then let the physician put the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and bandage, if pus does not form.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside first and then return to your work and care; the bandage is done in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, and let the extra material remain, then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg next to the knee below, and make the ends of the thread come up; then wrap around the leg and thigh the bandage, then place splints on the fracture, and place one splint on the bone of the leg; then apply a soft dressing between the thigh and leg made of soft cloths to keep the tension even, then begin to tightly bind three or four turns around the fracture; and as you go up the fracture, tighten less; then pay attention to the two ends of the thread that you put between the leg and thigh, and tie them with the three splints that are above, then return to the underside of the thread end, until you come next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, unless there comes a abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, loosen it, and realign what is coming out, as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of the bone that prick, they must be gouged out if possible; and if not, the place must be broken open and pulled out; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel pins are put in, as in the shoulder and arm; yet, with this kind of restoration, the patient does not fare well.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in 30 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the hollow of the knee there often occurs a small break, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and it happens with all wounds, with or without wound, and this one can feel well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one sets even what is dislocated at its joints, so that it can be moved as soon as possible; then applies the poultice and places a round bandage if necessary, and binds it as needed. Then consider all the precautions as we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar things; and for each symptom, do what is necessary, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by its proper name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it has all kinds of fractures as it happens in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the work is also identical.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns all around.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain and it is visible; and it turns upside down. Then provide traction, align it properly, and bind the splints evenly. However, if the fracture is severe with many pieces, then the traction should be less and more gentle, and support according to its severity.[Rest assured that I am not adding any comments or contextual information about the text, as per your instructions. Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two splints of shaved wood that extend around the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee downwards. Then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and bind it securely in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and this is good. And some provide a bed for the length of the leg made of wood to guard against movement, and it is properly done in cases where there is a wound.
